💾 Backup & Disaster Recovery
🔄 Automated Backup Strategy
# 1. Automated EBS Snapshots with DLM (Data Lifecycle Manager)
aws dlm create-lifecycle-policy \
    --execution-role-arn arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/AWSDataLifecycleManagerDefaultRole \
    --description "Daily snapshots for anihpj EC2 volumes" \
    --state ENABLED \
    --policy-details '{
        "ResourceTypes": ["VOLUME"],
        "TargetTags": [
            {"Key": "Project", "Value": "anihpj"}
        ],
        "Schedules": [
            {
                "Name": "Daily snapshots",
                "CreateRule": {
                    "Interval": 24,
                    "IntervalUnit": "HOURS",
                    "Times": ["03:00"]
                },
                "RetainRule": {
                    "Count": 7
                },
                "TagsToAdd": [
                    {"Key": "SnapshotType", "Value": "DailyBackup"}
                ],
                "CopyTags": true
            }
        ]
    }'

# 2. Create AMI for disaster recovery
aws ec2 create-image \
    --instance-id i-0abc123def456789 \
    --name "anihpj-backup-$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S)" \
    --description "Backup AMI for disaster recovery" \
    --no-reboot  # Don't reboot instance

# 3. Copy snapshots to different region (DR)
aws ec2 copy-snapshot \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-snapshot-id snap-0abc123def456789 \
    --destination-region us-west-2 \
    --description "DR snapshot for anihpj"
🚨 Disaster Recovery Plan
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         DISASTER RECOVERY TIERS FOR ANIHPJ                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  Tier 1: Backup & Restore (Lowest cost, slowest recovery)       │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  RTO: 24 hours  |  RPO: 24 hours                           │ │
│  │  • Daily EBS snapshots                                      │ │
│  │  • Daily database backups to S3                            │ │
│  │  • Restore from snapshots when disaster occurs             │ │
│  │  Cost: ~$50/month (storage only)                           │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Tier 2: Pilot Light (Medium cost, medium recovery)             │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  RTO: 1-2 hours  |  RPO: 1 hour                            │ │
│  │  • Minimal resources running in DR region                  │ │
│  │  • Database standby replica (read-only)                    │ │
│  │  • AMIs and snapshots ready                                │ │
│  │  • Scale up EC2 instances when disaster occurs             │ │
│  │  Cost: ~$200/month (small DB + snapshots)                  │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Tier 3: Warm Standby (Higher cost, faster recovery)            │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  RTO: 15-30 minutes  |  RPO: 5-15 minutes                  │ │
│  │  • Scaled-down version running in DR region                │ │
│  │  • 1 EC2 instance running (instead of 3)                   │ │
│  │  • Database with continuous replication                    │ │
│  │  • Route 53 health checks for automatic failover           │ │
│  │  Cost: ~$500/month                                          │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Tier 4: Hot Standby (Highest cost, fastest recovery)           │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  RTO: < 5 minutes  |  RPO: Real-time                       │ │
│  │  • Full production environment in DR region                │ │
│  │  • Active-active configuration                              │ │
│  │  • Route 53 distributes traffic to both regions            │ │
│  │  • Database with synchronous replication                   │ │
│  │  Cost: ~$1000/month (2× production costs)                  │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Recommendation for anihpj:                                     │
│  Start with Tier 2 (Pilot Light) - Best balance of cost/RTO    │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🏷️ Tagging Strategy
Consistent tagging is crucial for cost allocation, automation, and management.

Required Tags for anihpj:
┌─────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Tag Key         │ Example Value                            │
├─────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ Name            │ anihpj-web-server-01                     │
│ Project         │ anihpj                                   │
│ Environment     │ production / staging / development       │
│ Owner           │ devops-team@company.com                  │
│ CostCenter      │ engineering                              │
│ Application     │ job-portal                               │
│ ManagedBy       │ terraform / cloudformation / manual      │
│ BackupSchedule  │ daily / weekly / none                    │
│ DataClass       │ public / internal / confidential         │
│ ComplianceReq   │ none / pci-dss / hipaa / gdpr           │
└─────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────┘

# Apply tags using AWS CLI
aws ec2 create-tags \
    --resources i-0abc123def456789 \
    --tags \
        Key=Name,Value=anihpj-web-server-01 \
        Key=Project,Value=anihpj \
        Key=Environment,Value=production \
        Key=Owner,Value=devops@company.com \
        Key=CostCenter,Value=engineering

⚙️ Batch Processing
📊 Resume Parsing with AWS Batch
# Use case: Parse uploaded resumes in batch (PDF → structured data)
# Architecture: S3 upload → Lambda trigger → AWS Batch job

# jobpost/batch_processing.py
import boto3
import PyPDF2
import json
from datetime import datetime

def process_resume_batch(s3_bucket, s3_keys):
    """
    Process multiple resumes in batch
    Runs on EC2 Spot instances via AWS Batch
    """
    s3 = boto3.client('s3')
    results = []
    
    for key in s3_keys:
        try:
            # Download resume from S3
            response = s3.get_object(Bucket=s3_bucket, Key=key)
            pdf_content = response['Body'].read()
            
            # Parse PDF
            pdf_reader = PyPDF2.PdfReader(io.BytesIO(pdf_content))
            text = ''
            for page in pdf_reader.pages:
                text += page.extract_text()
            
            # Extract structured data (simplified)
            parsed_data = {
                'filename': key,
                'text': text,
                'email': extract_email(text),
                'phone': extract_phone(text),
                'skills': extract_skills(text),
                'experience_years': extract_experience(text),
                'processed_at': datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
            }
            
            # Store results in S3 or database
            result_key = key.replace('uploads/', 'parsed/').replace('.pdf', '.json')
            s3.put_object(
                Bucket=s3_bucket,
                Key=result_key,
                Body=json.dumps(parsed_data),
                ContentType='application/json'
            )
            
            results.append({'key': key, 'status': 'success'})
            
        except Exception as e:
            results.append({'key': key, 'status': 'error', 'error': str(e)})
    
    return results

# AWS Batch configuration
# Runs on Spot instances (70% cost savings)
# Scales from 0 to 100 instances based on queue depth
💻 Dev/Test Environments
# Cost-effective dev/test strategy for anihpj

# 1. Use smaller instance types
# Production: m5.large ($70/month)
# Dev/Test: t3.medium ($30/month) - Save $40/month

# 2. Use Spot Instances (save 70%)
# Dev/Test: t3.medium Spot ($9/month) - Save $61/month

# 3. Automate start/stop schedules
# Only run dev instances during business hours (8am-6pm, Mon-Fri)
# Cost: $9/month × 50 hours/week ÷ 168 hours/week = $2.68/month

# Lambda function to stop dev instances at 6pm
import boto3
from datetime import datetime

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    ec2 = boto3.client('ec2')
    
    # Stop all instances tagged Environment=development
    response = ec2.describe_instances(
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'tag:Environment', 'Values': ['development']},
            {'Name': 'instance-state-name', 'Values': ['running']}
        ]
    )
    
    instance_ids = []
    for reservation in response['Reservations']:
        for instance in reservation['Instances']:
            instance_ids.append(instance['InstanceId'])
    
    if instance_ids:
        ec2.stop_instances(InstanceIds=instance_ids)
        print(f"Stopped instances: {instance_ids}")
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Development instances stopped'}

# Schedule with EventBridge: 0 18 * * MON-FRI (6pm weekdays)

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

❌ Instance Won't Start
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         TROUBLESHOOTING: INSTANCE WON'T START                    │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  Problem: Instance stuck in "pending" state                      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Possible causes:                                           │ │
│  │  1. Insufficient capacity in Availability Zone              │ │
│  │  2. Instance limit reached                                  │ │
│  │  3. Invalid AMI                                             │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Solutions:                                                  │ │
│  │  • Try different Availability Zone                          │ │
│  │  • Request service limit increase                           │ │
│  │  • Verify AMI is available in your region                   │ │
│  │  • Check System Status and Instance Status checks           │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Problem: Instance failing status checks                         │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  System Status Check Failed (AWS infrastructure problem)   │ │
│  │  ✅ Solution: Stop and start instance (moves to new host)   │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Instance Status Check Failed (OS/application problem)      │ │
│  │  ✅ Solution: Check system logs, fix OS issues              │ │
│  │  • Incorrect network configuration                          │ │
│  │  • Kernel panic                                             │ │
│  │  • Out of memory                                            │ │
│  │  • Corrupt filesystem                                       │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Problem: Instance terminated unexpectedly                       │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Check termination reason:                                  │ │
│  │  • Spot Instance interrupted (check Spot request status)    │ │
│  │  • Auto Scaling scaled in (check ASG activity history)      │ │
│  │  • User terminated (check CloudTrail logs)                  │ │
│  │  • Health check failed (check ELB target health)            │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

# Check instance status
aws ec2 describe-instance-status --instance-ids i-0abc123def456789

# View system logs
aws ec2 get-console-output --instance-id i-0abc123def456789

# Reboot instance
aws ec2 reboot-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123def456789

# Stop and start (moves to new physical host)
aws ec2 stop-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123def456789
aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123def456789
🔌 Can't Connect to Instance
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         TROUBLESHOOTING: CONNECTION ISSUES                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  SSH Connection Timeout                                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  Checklist:                                                  │ │
│  │  ☐ Instance is running (not stopped/terminated)             │ │
│  │  ☐ Instance has public IP address                           │ │
│  │  ☐ Security Group allows inbound SSH (port 22)              │ │
│  │  ☐ Network ACL allows traffic                               │ │
│  │  ☐ Route table has route to Internet Gateway                │ │
│  │  ☐ Correct key pair is being used                           │ │
│  │  ☐ Key file permissions are correct (chmod 400)             │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Debug command:                                              │ │
│  │  ssh -vvv -i anihpj-keypair.pem ec2-user@1.2.3.4           │ │
│  │  (Verbose output shows where connection fails)              │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Permission Denied (publickey)                                   │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  • Wrong username (ec2-user for Amazon Linux, ubuntu for   │ │
│  │    Ubuntu, admin for Debian)                                │ │
│  │  • Wrong key pair                                           │ │
│  │  • Key file permissions too open (must be 400)              │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Fix key permissions:                                        │ │
│  │  chmod 400 anihpj-keypair.pem                               │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Application Not Accessible (HTTP/HTTPS)                         │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ☐ Security Group allows inbound port 80/443                │ │
│  │  ☐ Django is running (check with: ps aux | grep gunicorn)  │ │
│  │  ☐ Django is listening on 0.0.0.0 (not 127.0.0.1)          │ │
│  │  ☐ Firewall allows traffic (sudo iptables -L)               │ │
│  │  ☐ ALLOWED_HOSTS in Django settings includes EC2 IP         │ │
│  │                                                              │ │
│  │  Test locally on EC2:                                        │ │
│  │  curl http://localhost:8000                                  │ │
│  │  If works → Security Group issue                            │ │
│  │  If fails → Django configuration issue                      │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🐌 Performance Issues
📉 Diagnose Slow Performance
# 1. Check CPU utilization
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EC2 \
    --metric-name CPUUtilization \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Average,Maximum

# 2. Check memory usage (requires CloudWatch agent)
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace CWAgent \
    --metric-name mem_used_percent \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Average,Maximum

# 3. Check disk I/O
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EBS \
    --metric-name VolumeReadOps \
    --dimensions Name=VolumeId,Value=vol-0abc123def456789 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Sum

# 4. SSH into instance and run diagnostics
ssh -i anihpj-keypair.pem ec2-user@1.2.3.4

# Check CPU and memory
top -n 1

# Check disk usage
df -h

# Check disk I/O
iostat -x 1 5

# Check network
netstat -an | grep ESTABLISHED | wc -l  # Active connections

# Check Django logs
tail -f /var/log/anihpj/gunicorn.log
tail -f /var/log/anihpj/django.log

# Check slow queries in PostgreSQL
# Connect to RDS and run:
SELECT query, mean_exec_time, calls 
FROM pg_stat_statements 
ORDER BY mean_exec_time DESC 
LIMIT 10;
💰 Common FAQs
Q: Why am I being charged when my instance is stopped?
A: Stopped instances don't incur EC2 compute charges, but you're 
   still charged for:
   • EBS volumes attached to the instance
   • Elastic IP addresses not associated with running instances
   • Snapshots and AMIs
   
   Solution: Delete unused EBS volumes, release unused Elastic IPs

Q: What's the difference between Stop and Terminate?
A: • Stop: Instance is stopped, can be started again, data preserved
   • Terminate: Instance is permanently deleted, cannot be recovered
   
   Tip: Enable termination protection for production instances!

Q: Can I change instance type without losing data?
A: Yes! Stop the instance, change instance type, then start it.
   Data on EBS volumes is preserved.
   
   aws ec2 stop-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123
   aws ec2 modify-instance-attribute \
       --instance-id i-0abc123 \
       --instance-type m5.xlarge
   aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

Q: How do I transfer files to/from EC2?
A: Multiple options:
   • SCP: scp -i key.pem file.txt ec2-user@1.2.3.4:/home/ec2-user/
   • SFTP: sftp -i key.pem ec2-user@1.2.3.4
   • S3: Upload to S3, then download on EC2 (aws s3 cp)
   • rsync: rsync -avz -e "ssh -i key.pem" ...

Q: What happens to my data when instance is terminated?
A: • Root EBS volume: Deleted (unless DeleteOnTermination=false)
   • Additional EBS volumes: Preserved (unless explicitly deleted)
   • Instance Store: Permanently lost
   
   Always backup important data!

Q: Can I recover a terminated instance?
A: No, termination is permanent. However:
   • If you have EBS snapshots, create new instance from snapshot
   • If you have AMI backup, launch new instance from AMI
   • Check CloudTrail to see who terminated it and when

Q: How do I get a static IP for my EC2 instance?
A: Allocate and associate an Elastic IP:
   
   aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc
   aws ec2 associate-address \
       --instance-id i-0abc123 \
       --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

Q: Can I use EC2 without a VPC?
A: No, EC2-Classic has been retired. All EC2 instances must be 
   launched in a VPC (Virtual Private Cloud).

⌨️ API & CLI Quick Reference

🚀 Most Used EC2 Commands
# ========================================
# INSTANCE MANAGEMENT
# ========================================

# List all instances
aws ec2 describe-instances

# List running instances only
aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --filters "Name=instance-state-name,Values=running"

# List instances by tag
aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --filters "Name=tag:Project,Values=anihpj"

# Launch new instance
aws ec2 run-instances \
    --image-id ami-0c7217cdde317cfec \
    --instance-type t3.medium \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair \
    --security-group-ids sg-0abc123 \
    --subnet-id subnet-0abc123 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-web}]'

# Stop instance
aws ec2 stop-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Start instance
aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Reboot instance
aws ec2 reboot-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Terminate instance
aws ec2 terminate-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Change instance type (must be stopped first)
aws ec2 modify-instance-attribute \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --instance-type m5.large

# ========================================
# EBS VOLUME MANAGEMENT
# ========================================

# Create volume
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 50 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --encrypted

# Attach volume to instance
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123 \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --device /dev/sdf

# Detach volume
aws ec2 detach-volume --volume-id vol-0abc123

# Delete volume
aws ec2 delete-volume --volume-id vol-0abc123

# Create snapshot
aws ec2 create-snapshot \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123 \
    --description "anihpj backup 2024-01-15"

# Copy snapshot to another region
aws ec2 copy-snapshot \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-snapshot-id snap-0abc123 \
    --destination-region us-west-2

# ========================================
# SECURITY GROUPS
# ========================================

# Create security group
aws ec2 create-security-group \
    --group-name anihpj-web-sg \
    --description "Security group for anihpj web servers" \
    --vpc-id vpc-0abc123

# Add inbound rule (HTTP)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 80 \
    --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# Add inbound rule (HTTPS)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 443 \
    --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# Add inbound rule (SSH from specific IP)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 22 \
    --cidr 203.0.113.0/24

# Remove rule
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 22 \
    --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# ========================================
# ELASTIC IP
# ========================================

# Allocate Elastic IP
aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc

# Associate with instance
aws ec2 associate-address \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

# Disassociate from instance
aws ec2 disassociate-address \
    --association-id eipassoc-0abc123

# Release Elastic IP
aws ec2 release-address --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

# ========================================
# KEY PAIRS
# ========================================

# Create key pair (saves private key to file)
aws ec2 create-key-pair \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair-2024 \
    --query 'KeyMaterial' \
    --output text > anihpj-keypair-2024.pem
chmod 400 anihpj-keypair-2024.pem

# List key pairs
aws ec2 describe-key-pairs

# Delete key pair
aws ec2 delete-key-pair --key-name anihpj-old-keypair

# ========================================
# AMI MANAGEMENT
# ========================================

# Create AMI from instance
aws ec2 create-image \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --name "anihpj-golden-image-2024-01-15" \
    --description "Configured anihpj Django application" \
    --no-reboot

# Copy AMI to another region
aws ec2 copy-image \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-image-id ami-0abc123 \
    --region us-west-2 \
    --name "anihpj-golden-image-west"

# Delete AMI
aws ec2 deregister-image --image-id ami-0abc123

# ========================================
# MONITORING & LOGS
# ========================================

# Get instance console output
aws ec2 get-console-output --instance-id i-0abc123

# Get instance screenshot
aws ec2 get-console-screenshot --instance-id i-0abc123

# Describe instance status
aws ec2 describe-instance-status --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Enable detailed monitoring
aws ec2 monitor-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Disable detailed monitoring
aws ec2 unmonitor-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123
🐍 Python Boto3 Examples
# anihpj/management/commands/manage_ec2.py
import boto3
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand

class Command(BaseCommand):
    help = 'Manage EC2 instances for anihpj'
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__()
        self.ec2 = boto3.client('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
        self.ec2_resource = boto3.resource('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
    
    def add_arguments(self, parser):
        parser.add_argument('action', type=str, 
                          help='Action: list|start|stop|launch')
        parser.add_argument('--instance-id', type=str, 
                          help='Instance ID for start/stop actions')
    
    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        action = options['action']
        
        if action == 'list':
            self.list_instances()
        elif action == 'start':
            self.start_instance(options['instance_id'])
        elif action == 'stop':
            self.stop_instance(options['instance_id'])
        elif action == 'launch':
            self.launch_instance()
    
    def list_instances(self):
        """List all anihpj instances"""
        response = self.ec2.describe_instances(
            Filters=[
                {'Name': 'tag:Project', 'Values': ['anihpj']},
                {'Name': 'instance-state-name', 
                 'Values': ['running', 'stopped', 'stopping', 'pending']}
            ]
        )
        
        for reservation in response['Reservations']:
            for instance in reservation['Instances']:
                name = next((tag['Value'] for tag in instance.get('Tags', []) 
                           if tag['Key'] == 'Name'), 'N/A')
                
                self.stdout.write(
                    f"ID: {instance['InstanceId']}\n"
                    f"Name: {name}\n"
                    f"Type: {instance['InstanceType']}\n"
                    f"State: {instance['State']['Name']}\n"
                    f"IP: {instance.get('PublicIpAddress', 'N/A')}\n"
                    f"Launch Time: {instance['LaunchTime']}\n"
                    f"---"
                )
    
    def start_instance(self, instance_id):
        """Start stopped instance"""
        if not instance_id:
            self.stderr.write("Error: --instance-id required")
            return
        
        try:
            self.ec2.start_instances(InstanceIds=[instance_id])
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f"Started instance {instance_id}")
            )
        except Exception as e:
            self.stderr.write(f"Error starting instance: {str(e)}")
    
    def stop_instance(self, instance_id):
        """Stop running instance"""
        if not instance_id:
            self.stderr.write("Error: --instance-id required")
            return
        
        try:
            self.ec2.stop_instances(InstanceIds=[instance_id])
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f"Stopped instance {instance_id}")
            )
        except Exception as e:
            self.stderr.write(f"Error stopping instance: {str(e)}")
    
    def launch_instance(self):
        """Launch new anihpj web server"""
        try:
            instances = self.ec2_resource.create_instances(
                ImageId='ami-0c7217cdde317cfec',  # Amazon Linux 2023
                InstanceType='t3.medium',
                KeyName='anihpj-keypair',
                SecurityGroupIds=['sg-0abc123'],
                SubnetId='subnet-0abc123',
                MinCount=1,
                MaxCount=1,
                TagSpecifications=[
                    {
                        'ResourceType': 'instance',
                        'Tags': [
                            {'Key': 'Name', 'Value': 'anihpj-web-auto'},
                            {'Key': 'Project', 'Value': 'anihpj'},
                            {'Key': 'Environment', 'Value': 'production'},
                            {'Key': 'ManagedBy', 'Value': 'django-command'}
                        ]
                    }
                ],
                IamInstanceProfile={'Name': 'anihpj-ec2-profile'},
                UserData=self.get_user_data()
            )
            
            instance_id = instances[0].id
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f"Launched instance {instance_id}")
            )
            
            # Wait for instance to be running
            self.stdout.write("Waiting for instance to start...")
            instances[0].wait_until_running()
            instances[0].reload()
            
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(
                    f"Instance running at {instances[0].public_ip_address}"
                )
            )
            
        except Exception as e:
            self.stderr.write(f"Error launching instance: {str(e)}")
    
    def get_user_data(self):
        """Get user data script for instance initialization"""
        return '''#!/bin/bash
        yum update -y
        yum install -y python3 python3-pip git
        pip3 install django gunicorn psycopg2-binary boto3
        
        # Clone anihpj repository
        cd /opt
        git clone https://github.com/your-org/anihpj.git
        cd anihpj
        
        # Install Python dependencies
        pip3 install -r requirements.txt
        
        # Set environment variables
        export DATABASE_URL="postgresql://..."
        export SECRET_KEY="..."
        
        # Run migrations
        python3 manage.py migrate
        
        # Collect static files
        python3 manage.py collectstatic --noinput
        
        # Start Gunicorn
        gunicorn anihpj.wsgi:application --bind 0.0.0.0:8000 --workers 4 --daemon
        '''

# Usage:
# python manage.py manage_ec2 list
# python manage.py manage_ec2 start --instance-id i-0abc123
# python manage.py manage_ec2 stop --instance-id i-0abc123
# python manage.py manage_ec2 launch

🔗 Integration with AWS Services

📦 S3 Integration for Static Files
# settings.py - Configure Django to use S3 for static/media files
import os

# S3 Configuration
AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID = os.environ.get('AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID')
AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY = os.environ.get('AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY')
AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME = 'anihpj-static'
AWS_S3_REGION_NAME = 'us-east-1'
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = f'{AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME}.s3.amazonaws.com'

# Static files (CSS, JavaScript, Images)
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/static/'
STATICFILES_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'

# Media files (User uploads)
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/media/'
DEFAULT_FILE_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'

# S3 object parameters
AWS_S3_OBJECT_PARAMETERS = {
    'CacheControl': 'max-age=86400',  # 1 day cache
}

# Security
AWS_DEFAULT_ACL = 'public-read'
AWS_S3_FILE_OVERWRITE = False
AWS_QUERYSTRING_AUTH = False  # Don't add auth to URLs
🗄️ RDS Database Integration
# settings.py - Configure Django to use RDS PostgreSQL
import os
import dj_database_url

# Parse DATABASE_URL environment variable
DATABASES = {
    'default': dj_database_url.config(
        default=os.environ.get('DATABASE_URL'),
        conn_max_age=600,
        conn_health_checks=True,
        ssl_require=True
    )
}

# Alternative explicit configuration
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj',
        'USER': 'anihpj_admin',
        'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD'),
        'HOST': 'anihpj-db.abc123.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com',
        'PORT': '5432',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'sslmode': 'require',
            'connect_timeout': 10,
        },
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,  # Connection pooling
    }
}

# Read replica for reporting queries
DATABASES['read_replica'] = {
    'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
    'NAME': 'anihpj',
    'USER': 'anihpj_readonly',
    'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD_READONLY'),
    'HOST': 'anihpj-db-replica.abc123.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com',
    'PORT': '5432',
    'OPTIONS': {'sslmode': 'require'},
}

# Database router for read/write splitting
class DatabaseRouter:
    def db_for_read(self, model, **hints):
        """Send read queries to replica"""
        return 'read_replica'
    
    def db_for_write(self, model, **hints):
        """Send write queries to primary"""
        return 'default'

DATABASE_ROUTERS = ['anihpj.settings.DatabaseRouter']

# jobpost/views.py - Send job application emails
from django.core.mail import send_mail

def apply_job(request, job_id):
    job = JobPost.objects.get(id=job_id)
    applicant_email = request.POST.get('email')
    resume = request.FILES.get('resume')
    
    # Send confirmation to applicant
    send_mail(
        subject=f'Application Received: {job.title}',
        message=f'Thank you for applying to {job.title} at {job.author.company}.',
        from_email='noreply@anihpj.com',
        recipient_list=[applicant_email],
        fail_silently=False,
    )
    
    # Notify employer
    send_mail(
        subject=f'New Application: {job.title}',
        message=f'New application from {applicant_email}',
        from_email='noreply@anihpj.com',
        recipient_list=[job.author.user.email],
        fail_silently=False,
    )
🔍 CloudWatch Logs Integration
# Install CloudWatch logs agent
# settings.py - Configure Django logging to CloudWatch
import boto3
from botocore.config import Config

LOGGING = {
    'version': 1,
    'disable_existing_loggers': False,
    'handlers': {
        'cloudwatch': {
            'level': 'INFO',
            'class': 'watchtower.CloudWatchLogHandler',
            'boto3_client': boto3.client(
                'logs',
                region_name='us-east-1',
                config=Config(retries={'max_attempts': 10, 'mode': 'standard'})
            ),
            'log_group_name': '/aws/ec2/anihpj',
            'log_stream_name': '{instance_id}-django',
        },
        'console': {
            'class': 'logging.StreamHandler',
        },
    },
    'root': {
        'handlers': ['console', 'cloudwatch'],
        'level': 'INFO',
    },
    'loggers': {
        'django': {
            'handlers': ['console', 'cloudwatch'],
            'level': 'INFO',
            'propagate': False,
        },
    },
}

🚚 Migration to EC2

🏠 On-Premises to AWS EC2
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│         MIGRATION STRATEGY: ON-PREMISES → AWS EC2                │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                  │
│  Phase 1: Assessment & Planning (2-4 weeks)                      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ☐ Inventory applications and dependencies                  │ │
│  │  ☐ Assess performance requirements                          │ │
│  │  ☐ Calculate costs (TCO comparison)                         │ │
│  │  ☐ Identify dependencies and integration points             │ │
│  │  ☐ Plan network architecture (VPC, subnets)                 │ │
│  │  ☐ Define security requirements                             │ │
│  │  ☐ Create migration timeline                                │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Phase 2: Proof of Concept (2-3 weeks)                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ☐ Set up AWS account and IAM                               │ │
│  │  ☐ Create VPC and networking                                │ │
│  │  ☐ Deploy test anihpj instance                              │ │
│  │  ☐ Migrate sample database                                  │ │
│  │  ☐ Test application functionality                           │ │
│  │  ☐ Performance testing                                      │ │
│  │  ☐ Validate backup/recovery procedures                      │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Phase 3: Migration Execution (1-2 weeks)                        │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ☐ Set up production environment                            │ │
│  │  ☐ Configure Auto Scaling and Load Balancing                │ │
│  │  ☐ Migrate database (use AWS DMS if needed)                 │ │
│  │  ☐ Sync static files to S3                                  │ │
│  │  ☐ Deploy application code                                  │ │
│  │  ☐ Configure monitoring and alerts                          │ │
│  │  ☐ Update DNS records                                       │ │
│  │  ☐ Run parallel for cutover period                          │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Phase 4: Post-Migration (Ongoing)                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │  ☐ Monitor performance and costs                            │ │
│  │  ☐ Optimize resource utilization                            │ │
│  │  ☐ Implement cost optimization strategies                   │ │
│  │  ☐ Train team on AWS operations                             │ │
│  │  ☐ Document architecture and procedures                     │ │
│  │  ☐ Decommission on-premises infrastructure                  │ │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ │
│                                                                  │
│  Migration Tools:                                                │
│  • AWS Application Migration Service (MGN) - Lift-and-shift     │
│  • AWS Database Migration Service (DMS) - Database migration    │
│  • AWS DataSync - Large data transfers                          │
│  • AWS Snow Family - Petabyte-scale data transfer               │
│                                                                  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

🛡️ Compliance & Governance

📜 Compliance Certifications
AWS EC2 Compliance & Certifications:

✅ SOC 1/2/3 - Service Organization Control
✅ PCI DSS Level 1 - Payment Card Industry
✅ ISO 27001/27017/27018 - Information Security
✅ HIPAA - Healthcare Insurance Portability
✅ GDPR - General Data Protection Regulation
✅ FedRAMP - Federal Risk Authorization Program
✅ FISMA - Federal Information Security Management
✅ IRAP - Australian Government (Certified)
✅ MTCS - Multi-Tier Cloud Security (Singapore)
✅ C5 - Cloud Computing Compliance Controls (Germany)

For anihpj Job Portal:
• GDPR compliance required if serving EU users
• Data encryption at rest (EBS) and in transit (HTTPS)
• Regular security audits and penetration testing
• User data access controls and logging (CloudTrail)
• Right to erasure (delete user data on request)
🔐 Security Best Practices Summary
AWS Well-Architected Framework - Security Pillar:

1. Identity & Access Management
   ✓ Use IAM roles (never store credentials on EC2)
   ✓ Enable MFA for root and admin accounts
   ✓ Apply least privilege principle
   ✓ Rotate credentials regularly

2. Detective Controls
   ✓ Enable CloudTrail for audit logging
   ✓ Enable VPC Flow Logs
   ✓ Use GuardDuty for threat detection
   ✓ Set up CloudWatch alarms

3. Infrastructure Protection
   ✓ Use Security Groups and NACLs
   ✓ Deploy in private subnets where possible
   ✓ Use AWS WAF for web application firewall
   ✓ Enable DDoS protection (Shield)

4. Data Protection
   ✓ Encrypt data at rest (EBS, RDS, S3)
   ✓ Encrypt data in transit (HTTPS, TLS)
   ✓ Use AWS KMS for key management
   ✓ Regular backups and snapshots

5. Incident Response
   ✓ Documented incident response plan
   ✓ Automated remediation where possible
   ✓ Regular security drills
   ✓ Post-incident analysis and improvements

📖 Glossary

Key EC2 Terms:

AMI (Amazon Machine Image)
    Pre-configured template for EC2 instances containing OS and software.

Auto Scaling
    Automatically adjust the number of EC2 instances based on demand.

Availability Zone (AZ)
    Isolated data center within an AWS Region. Each Region has multiple AZs.

EBS (Elastic Block Store)
    Persistent block storage for EC2 instances (like a hard drive).

EC2 (Elastic Compute Cloud)
    Virtual servers in the AWS cloud.

Elastic IP
    Static IPv4 address designed for dynamic cloud computing.

IAM (Identity and Access Management)
    Service for managing access to AWS resources.

Instance
    A virtual server in Amazon EC2.

Instance Store
    Temporary block storage physically attached to host computer.

Launch Template
    Configuration template for launching EC2 instances.

Reserved Instance
    Purchase option with discounted hourly rate for 1 or 3-year commitment.

Security Group
    Virtual firewall controlling inbound and outbound traffic to instances.

Snapshot
    Point-in-time backup of an EBS volume.

Spot Instance
    Spare EC2 capacity available at up to 90% discount.

User Data
    Scripts or commands that run when an instance starts.

VPC (Virtual Private Cloud)
    Isolated virtual network where you launch AWS resources.

─────
• January: M7i instances (Intel Sapphire Rapids)
• February: Graviton4-based R8g instances

• Q2: M7g instances (general-purpose Graviton3)
• Q1: Trn1n instances (100GB networking for ML training)

2022
─────
• Q4: C7g instances (compute-optimized Graviton3)
• Q3: G5g instances (GPU with Graviton2)
• Q2: I4i instances (storage-optimized with NVMe SSD)
• Q1: X2idn, X2iedn instances (memory-optimized)

Instance Type Evolution:
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ T1 (2010) → T2 (2014) → T3 (2018) → T3a (2019)          │
│ M1 (2006) → M3 (2012) → M4 (2015) → M5 (2017) → M7g (2023) │
│ C1 (2008) → C3 (2013) → C4 (2015) → C5 (2017) → C7g (2022) │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Key Feature Additions:
• 2023: EC2 Instance Connect Endpoint (secure access without public IPs)
• 2022: Nitro Enclaves (isolated compute environments)
• 2021: Mac instances (macOS on EC2)
• 2020: Graviton2 processors (ARM-based, better price/performance)
• 2019: Inf1 instances (ML inference with AWS Inferentia chips)
• 2018: Elastic Fabric Adapter (EFA) for HPC workloads

For anihpj Job Portal:
• Recommended: Use latest generation (M7g, T3, C7g)
• Benefits: Better performance, lower cost, modern features
• Migration: Easy to change instance types (stop → modify → start)

AWS Lambda

Category: Compute (Serverless)  |  Use Case: Event-Driven Applications, APIs, Background Tasks  |  Pricing: Pay-per-request, Free Tier Available  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS Lambda Docs

Serverless compute service that runs your code in response to events and automatically manages compute resources. Perfect for building scalable, event-driven applications without managing servers.

📋 Overview & Introduction

AWS Lambda is a serverless, event-driven compute service that lets you run code for virtually any type of application or backend service without provisioning or managing servers. Lambda runs your code only when needed and scales automatically from a few requests per day to thousands per second.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • No Server Management: No servers to provision, maintain, or manage
  • Automatic Scaling: Scales automatically from 0 to thousands of concurrent executions
  • Pay-per-Use: Only pay for compute time consumed (no idle charges)
  • High Availability: Built-in fault tolerance and redundancy across AZs
  • Event-Driven: Responds to events from 200+ AWS services and SaaS apps
  • Cost-Effective: 1M free requests/month + generous free tier compute time
  • Multiple Runtimes: Supports Python, Node.js, Java, Go, Ruby, .NET, custom runtimes
💡 When to Use Lambda for anihpj: Perfect for your Django job portal's background tasks (email notifications, report generation), API endpoints (REST APIs via API Gateway), scheduled jobs (cleanup tasks, data aggregation), and event-driven workflows (image processing, file uploads to S3).
⚖️ Lambda vs. Other Compute Services
Lambda: Serverless, event-driven, millisecond billing, auto-scale
EC2: Full control, persistent, always running, manual scaling
Fargate: Serverless containers, longer running tasks
ECS/EKS: Container orchestration, complex apps
Elastic Beanstalk: Managed platform, web apps with servers
App Runner: Container-based web apps, simplified
🏗️ Lambda in AWS Ecosystem - Architecture Overview
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        AWS SERVERLESS ECOSYSTEM                      │
│                                                                      │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ │
│  │                    EVENT SOURCES (Triggers)                     │ │
│  │                                                                 │ │
│  │  API Gateway    S3 Buckets    DynamoDB    EventBridge    SQS   │ │
│  │     │              │              │            │            │   │ │
│  │     │              │              │            │            │   │ │
│  │     └──────────────┴──────────────┴────────────┴────────────┘   │ │
│  │                            │                                     │ │
│  │                            ▼                                     │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │              AWS LAMBDA FUNCTION                          │  │ │
│  │  │         (anihpj-job-notification-sender)                  │  │ │
│  │  │                                                           │  │ │
│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  Python Handler Function                        │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  ┌───────────────────────────────────┐          │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  │  def lambda_handler(event, context): │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  │    # Your Django-related code     │          │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  │    # Process job post             │          │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  │    # Send notifications           │          │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  │    return response                │          │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  └───────────────────────────────────┘          │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │                                                  │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  Environment Variables:                         │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  - DB_HOST, DB_PASSWORD                         │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  - SES_SENDER_EMAIL                             │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │                                                  │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  IAM Execution Role:                            │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  - Access to RDS                                │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  - Access to SES                                │     │  │ │
│  │  │  │  - CloudWatch Logs                              │     │  │ │
│  │  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │  │ │
│  │  │                                                           │  │ │
│  │  │  Memory: 512 MB  |  Timeout: 30s  |  Runtime: Python 3.12 │  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  │                            │                                     │ │
│  │                            ▼                                     │ │
│  │  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │ │
│  │  │              AWS SERVICES (Destinations)                  │  │ │
│  │  │                                                           │  │ │
│  │  │  RDS/Aurora    S3 Storage    SES Email    CloudWatch     │  │ │
│  │  │  (Job Data)    (Reports)     (Notify)     (Logs/Metrics) │  │ │
│  │  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │ │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                                     │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  Lambda Layers (Shared Code)                               │   │
│  │  - Django ORM utilities                                    │   │
│  │  │  - Custom Python packages                                    │   │
│  │  - Common dependencies                                     │   │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
│                                                                     │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │
│  │  CloudWatch (Monitoring)                                   │   │
│  │  - Invocation count, duration, errors                      │   │
│  │  - Custom metrics and alarms                               │   │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Typical Flow for anihpj Job Portal:
1. User creates job post → DynamoDB Stream triggers Lambda
2. Lambda processes job data, extracts skills/location
3. Lambda queries RDS for matching candidates
4. Lambda sends email notifications via SES
5. Lambda logs results to CloudWatch
6. All done in seconds, no servers to manage!

🔧 Core Concepts

⚡ Lambda Functions

A Lambda function is the fundamental unit of Lambda. It contains your code and configuration that defines how Lambda processes events.

📊 Lambda Function Anatomy
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              AWS LAMBDA FUNCTION STRUCTURE                   │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                              │
│  Function Name: anihpj-job-notifier                         │
│  Runtime: Python 3.12                                        │
│  Handler: lambda_function.lambda_handler                     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Function Code (lambda_function.py)                │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │  import json                                       │     │
│  │  import boto3                                      │     │
│  │  import os                                         │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │  def lambda_handler(event, context):               │     │
│  │      """Main entry point"""                        │     │
│  │      # event = input data from trigger            │     │
│  │      # context = runtime information              │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │      print(f"Processing: {event}")                │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │      # Your business logic here                   │     │
│  │      result = process_job_post(event)             │     │
│  │                                                     │     │
│  │      return {                                      │     │
│  │          'statusCode': 200,                        │     │
│  │          'body': json.dumps(result)               │     │
│  │      }                                             │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Configuration                                      │     │
│  │  ├─ Memory: 512 MB (128 MB - 10,240 MB)           │     │
│  │  ├─ Timeout: 30 seconds (max 15 minutes)          │     │
│  │  ├─ Environment Variables:                         │     │
│  │  │   • DB_HOST=anihpj-db.amazonaws.com            │     │
│  │  │   • DB_PASSWORD=         │     │
│  │  │   • SES_SENDER=noreply@anihpj.com              │     │
│  │  ├─ IAM Execution Role: anihpj-lambda-role        │     │
│  │  ├─ VPC: vpc-12345 (if RDS access needed)         │     │
│  │  └─ Layers: [django-utils-layer, psycopg2-layer]  │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Triggers (Event Sources)                          │     │
│  │  ├─ API Gateway (HTTP POST /jobs)                  │     │
│  │  ├─ EventBridge (Schedule: rate(1 hour))           │     │
│  │  ├─ S3 (Object created in anihpj-uploads/)         │     │
│  │  └─ DynamoDB Stream (Jobs table changes)           │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
│                                                              │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐     │
│  │  Destinations (On Success/Failure)                 │     │
│  │  ├─ Success → SQS queue for further processing    │     │
│  │  └─ Failure → SNS topic for alerts                │     │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🚀 Invocation Types

Lambda supports three invocation types, each suited for different use cases:

📡 Three Lambda Invocation Models
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    INVOCATION TYPES                            │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  1️⃣ SYNCHRONOUS (Request-Response)                            │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Client → Lambda → Processing → Response → Client    │    │
│  │          ↓                            ↑               │    │
│  │          └────── Waits for result ────┘               │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  Use Cases:                                                    │
│  • API Gateway requests (REST APIs)                            │
│  • Mobile/web app direct invocations                           │
│  • Real-time data transformations                              │
│  • User-facing operations (must wait for response)             │
│                                                                │
│  Example: GET /api/jobs/{id}                                   │
│  Client waits for job details to be returned                   │
│                                                                │
│  Max Duration: 15 minutes                                      │
│  Retry: Client responsible                                     │
│                                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  2️⃣ ASYNCHRONOUS (Fire-and-Forget)                            │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Client → Lambda → 202 Accepted                       │    │
│  │              ↓                                        │    │
│  │              └─→ Queue → Process → Done               │    │
│  │                   (happens later)                     │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  Use Cases:                                                    │
│  • S3 events (file uploaded → process later)                   │
│  • SNS/EventBridge triggers                                    │
│  • Background tasks (email sending, reports)                   │
│  • Non-critical operations (can delay response)                │
│                                                                │
│  Example: S3 file upload → Lambda processes image              │
│  User doesn't wait for processing to complete                  │
│                                                                │
│  Max Duration: 15 minutes                                      │
│  Retry: Automatic (2 times by Lambda)                          │
│  Dead Letter Queue: Can configure for failed invocations       │
│                                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  3️⃣ POLL-BASED (Event Source Mapping)                         │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Lambda polls → SQS/Kinesis → Fetches batch          │    │
│  │                    ↓                                  │    │
│  │                    Process batch → ACK/NACK           │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  Use Cases:                                                    │
│  • SQS queues (batch message processing)                       │
│  • Kinesis/DynamoDB Streams (stream processing)                │
│  • Kafka topics (MSK integration)                              │
│  • High-throughput event processing                            │
│                                                                │
│  Example: SQS queue with 1000 job application messages         │
│  Lambda processes in batches of 10                             │
│                                                                │
│  Max Duration: 15 minutes                                      │
│  Retry: Depends on source (SQS: message visibility)            │
│  Batch Size: Configurable (1-10,000 for SQS)                   │
│                                                                │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

For anihpj Job Portal:
✓ Synchronous: REST API endpoints (search jobs, get details)
✓ Asynchronous: Email notifications, report generation
✓ Poll-based: Process application queue, analytics pipeline
📡 Event Sources (Triggers)

Lambda functions are triggered by events from various AWS services. Here are the most common event sources for Django applications:

🎯 Common Event Sources for anihpj
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│               EVENT SOURCES & USE CASES                        │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  📬 API GATEWAY (HTTP/REST APIs)                               │
│  ├─ Invocation: Synchronous                                    │
│  ├─ Use Case: RESTful API backend for mobile/web              │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      GET  /api/jobs → Lambda lists jobs                        │
│      POST /api/jobs → Lambda creates job post                  │
│      PUT  /api/jobs/{id} → Lambda updates job                  │
│                                                                │
│  📦 S3 (Object Events)                                         │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Triggers: s3:ObjectCreated, s3:ObjectRemoved              │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Upload resume.pdf → Lambda processes & extracts text      │
│      Upload company-logo.png → Lambda creates thumbnails       │
│                                                                │
│  📨 SQS (Message Queues)                                       │
│  ├─ Invocation: Poll-based (Event Source Mapping)             │
│  ├─ Batch Size: 1-10 messages per invocation                  │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Job applications queue → Lambda sends notifications       │
│      Email sending queue → Lambda dispatches via SES           │
│                                                                │
│  🔔 SNS (Pub/Sub Notifications)                                │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Fan-out: One message → Multiple Lambdas                    │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      New job posted → SNS topic → Lambda notifies subscribers  │
│                                                                │
│  ⏰ EventBridge (Scheduled Events)                             │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Schedule: Cron expressions or rate expressions            │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      rate(1 hour) → Lambda cleans up expired job posts         │
│      cron(0 9 * * ? *) → Lambda sends daily digest at 9 AM    │
│                                                                │
│  💾 DynamoDB Streams                                           │
│  ├─ Invocation: Poll-based (Event Source Mapping)             │
│  ├─ Change Data Capture: INSERT, MODIFY, REMOVE               │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Job post created → Stream → Lambda updates search index   │
│      Application submitted → Stream → Lambda triggers workflow │
│                                                                │
│  🗄️ RDS Events (via EventBridge)                               │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Events: DB instance events, automated backups             │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      DB snapshot completed → Lambda verifies backup integrity  │
│                                                                │
│  📊 CloudWatch Logs                                            │
│  ├─ Invocation: Asynchronous                                   │
│  ├─ Trigger: Log patterns matching                            │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      Error log detected → Lambda sends alert to Slack          │
│                                                                │
│  🔗 Application Load Balancer (ALB)                            │
│  ├─ Invocation: Synchronous                                    │
│  ├─ Use Case: Alternative to API Gateway                       │
│  └─ Example:                                                   │
│      ALB target group → Lambda handles HTTP requests           │
│                                                                │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
🏗️ Execution Environment

Understanding Lambda's execution environment is crucial for building efficient functions.

🔄 Lambda Execution Lifecycle
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│            LAMBDA EXECUTION ENVIRONMENT LIFECYCLE              │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                │
│  PHASE 1: INIT (Cold Start) - Happens once per container      │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  1. Download function code from S3                    │    │
│  │  2. Start execution environment (container)           │    │
│  │  3. Initialize runtime (Python 3.12)                  │    │
│  │  4. Load layers (if any)                              │    │
│  │  5. Execute INIT code (outside handler)               │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │     # Code outside handler runs ONCE                  │    │
│  │     import boto3                                      │    │
│  │     db_client = boto3.client('rds-data')  # Reused!  │    │
│  │     s3_client = boto3.client('s3')         # Reused!  │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │  Duration: 100ms - 2000ms (variable)                  │    │
│  │  Billed: Yes (since January 2024)                     │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
│  PHASE 2: INVOKE (Warm Execution) - Runs for each request     │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  1. Lambda receives event                             │    │
│  │  2. Execute handler function                          │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │     def lambda_handler(event, context):               │    │
│  │         # This runs for EVERY invocation             │    │
│  │         job_data = event['body']                     │    │
│  │         result = process_job(job_data)               │    │
│  │         return response                               │    │
│  │     ↓                                                 │    │
│  │  3. Return response                                   │    │
│  │  Duration: Your function execution time               │    │
│  │  Billed: Yes (per ms of execution)                    │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                     │                                          │
│                     ▼                                          │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Container stays warm for ~5-15 minutes               │    │
│  │  (Next invocation = no INIT phase = faster!)          │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                     │                                          │
│                     ▼                                          │
│  PHASE 3: SHUTDOWN (If no requests)                           │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐    │
│  │  Container destroyed after idle timeout                │    │
│  │  Next invocation = Cold Start again                    │    │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘    │
│                                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  OPTIMIZATION TIP:                                             │
│  ✓ Initialize connections OUTSIDE handler (reused across)     │
│  ✓ Use /tmp for temporary files (512 MB - 10 GB available)    │
│  ✓ Reuse container state between invocations                   │
│  ✗ Don't assume container persists (may be destroyed anytime)  │
├───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
💻 Cold Start vs. Warm Start Example
# lambda_function.py
import json
import boto3
import psycopg2
import os

# ============================================
# INIT PHASE CODE (Runs once per container)
# ============================================
print("INIT: Initializing connections...")

# These clients are created once and reused!
s3_client = boto3.client('s3')
ses_client = boto3.client('ses')

# Database connection (reused for warm starts)
DB_CONFIG = {
    'host': os.environ['DB_HOST'],
    'database': 'anihpj',
    'user': os.environ['DB_USER'],
    'password': os.environ['DB_PASSWORD']
}

# Don't open connection here! 
# Open when needed, connection pooling recommended
print("INIT: Configuration loaded")

# ============================================
# INVOKE PHASE CODE (Runs every invocation)
# ============================================
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """
    Handler function - executes for every request
    Duration impacts cost directly
    """
    print("INVOKE: Processing request...")
    
    # Parse incoming job post data
    job_data = json.loads(event['body'])
    
    # Connect to database (with retry logic)
    conn = psycopg2.connect(**DB_CONFIG)
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    
    try:
        # Insert job post into anihpj database
        cursor.execute("""
            INSERT INTO jobpost_jobpost 
            (title, description, company, location, salary_min, salary_max)
            VALUES (%s, %s, %s, %s, %s, %s)
            RETURNING id
        """, (
            job_data['title'],
            job_data['description'],
            job_data['company'],
            job_data['location'],
            job_data['salary_min'],
            job_data['salary_max']
        ))
        
        job_id = cursor.fetchone()[0]
        conn.commit()
        
        # Send notification email via SES (non-blocking)
        ses_client.send_email(
            Source='noreply@anihpj.com',
            Destination={'ToAddresses': ['admin@anihpj.com']},
            Message={
                'Subject': {'Data': f'New Job Posted: {job_data["title"]}'},
                'Body': {'Text': {'Data': f'Job ID: {job_id}'}}
            }
        )
        
        return {
            'statusCode': 201,
            'headers': {'Content-Type': 'application/json'},
            'body': json.dumps({
                'message': 'Job created successfully',
                'job_id': job_id
            })
        }
        
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"ERROR: {str(e)}")
        conn.rollback()
        return {
            'statusCode': 500,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': str(e)})
        }
        
    finally:
        cursor.close()
        conn.close()

# Execution Times:
# Cold Start: INIT (500ms) + INVOKE (200ms) = 700ms total
# Warm Start: INVOKE (200ms) only = 200ms total
# Savings: 71% faster on warm starts!

Before creating your first Lambda function for anihpj:

   • Basic Python programming

🎯 Create First Function
Simple Lambda for anihpj Job Notifications
import json
import boto3
from datetime import datetime

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """Send job notification email via SES"""
    
    job_data = json.loads(event['body'])
    ses_client = boto3.client('ses')
    
    ses_client.send_email(
        Source='noreply@anihpj.com',
        Destination={'ToAddresses': [job_data['subscriber_email']]},
        Message={
            'Subject': {'Data': f"New Job: {job_data['title']}"},
            'Body': {'Text': {'Data': f"Check out this opportunity at {job_data['company']}"}}
        }
    )
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Email sent'}
🧪 Testing & Debugging
💡 Quick Testing: Use AWS Console test events, AWS SAM CLI for local testing, or CloudWatch Logs for debugging production issues.

🔑 Key Features

⚡ Triggers & Event Sources

Lambda integrates with 200+ AWS services. Common triggers for anihpj: API Gateway (REST APIs), S3 (file uploads), EventBridge (scheduled tasks), SQS (message queues), DynamoDB Streams (data changes).

📦 Lambda Layers

Package dependencies separately from code. Create layers for common libraries (psycopg2, Django, boto3) and reuse across multiple functions. Max 5 layers per function, 250 MB total size limit.

🔧 Environment Variables
import os

# Access environment variables
db_host = os.environ['DB_HOST']
db_password = os.environ['DB_PASSWORD']

# Best practice: Use Secrets Manager for sensitive data
import boto3
secrets = boto3.client('secretsmanager')
secret = secrets.get_secret_value(SecretId='anihpj/db-password')
password = json.loads(secret['SecretString'])['password']
🌐 VPC Configuration

Connect Lambda to VPC for RDS database access. Configure subnets (use private), security groups, and ensure NAT Gateway or VPC Endpoints for internet access. Note: VPC increases cold start time by 1-2 seconds.

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

💵 Pricing Model
Lambda Pricing (2025):
• Requests: First 1M/month FREE, then $0.20 per 1M
• Compute: 400,000 GB-seconds/month FREE, then $0.0000166667 per GB-second
• Formula: (Memory in GB) × (Duration in seconds) = GB-seconds

Example: 1M requests, 512 MB, 200ms each
• Requests: FREE (within 1M limit)
• Compute: 1M × 0.5 GB × 0.2s = 100,000 GB-seconds → FREE
• Total: $0.00 🎉
💡 Cost Optimization
Top Optimization Strategies:
✅ Right-size memory (use Lambda Power Tuning tool)
✅ Reduce execution time (optimize code, reuse connections)
✅ Use Graviton2 (ARM64) for 20% cost savings
✅ Batch processing (10 messages/invocation vs 1)
✅ Minimize package size (faster cold starts)
✅ Use asynchronous invocation for non-critical tasks
✅ Monitor with CloudWatch, set cost alarms
📊 Cost Calculator
💡 Estimate: For anihpj with 5M requests/month, 512MB, 300ms avg duration: ~$25/month. Use AWS Pricing Calculator for precise estimates.

📈 Performance & Scalability

🔄 Concurrency & Scaling
Lambda Concurrency:
• Default: 1000 concurrent executions per region (soft limit)
• Automatic scaling: 0 to 1000s in seconds
• Reserved concurrency: Guarantee capacity for critical functions
• Provisioned concurrency: Pre-warm containers (eliminates cold starts)

For anihpj:
• Peak traffic: 100 requests/second
• Avg duration: 300ms
• Concurrent executions needed: 100 × 0.3 = 30
• Well within limits! ✓
❄️ Cold Starts
Cold Start Optimization:
• Cold start: ~500ms-2000ms (first invocation)
• Warm start: <10ms (subsequent invocations)

Mitigation Strategies:
✅ Keep functions warm with scheduled pings (EventBridge every 5 min)
✅ Use Provisioned Concurrency for critical endpoints
✅ Minimize package size (< 10 MB)
✅ Initialize connections outside handler
✅ Use Graviton2 (faster startup)
✅ Avoid VPC if possible (adds 1-2s to cold start)
⚡ Performance Tuning
# Performance Best Practices for anihpj Lambda

# 1. Initialize outside handler (reused across invocations)
import boto3
import psycopg2

s3_client = boto3.client('s3')  # ✅ Reused
db_conn_pool = create_connection_pool()  # ✅ Reused

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # 2. Use connection pooling
    conn = db_conn_pool.getconn()
    
    # 3. Parallel processing with threads
    from concurrent.futures import ThreadPoolExecutor
    with ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=10) as executor:
        results = executor.map(process_job, job_list)
    
    # 4. Use async/await for I/O operations
    import asyncio
    results = await asyncio.gather(*[fetch_data(url) for url in urls])
    
    # 5. Cache frequently accessed data
    cached_data = get_from_cache() or fetch_and_cache()
    
    db_conn_pool.putconn(conn)
    return {'statusCode': 200}

🎓 Advanced Topics

🐳 Container Images

Deploy Lambda functions as container images (up to 10 GB). Supports custom base images, easier local testing, familiar Docker workflow. Ideal for functions with large dependencies.

🔌 Lambda Extensions

Integrate monitoring tools (Datadog, New Relic), secrets fetching, logging without code changes. Extensions run in separate processes alongside your function.

⚙️ Provisioned Concurrency

Pre-warm execution environments to eliminate cold starts. Critical for latency-sensitive APIs. Cost: $0.000004167 per GB-second (on top of regular pricing). Use for peak hours only to optimize costs.

🎯 Destinations

Route function results to SQS, SNS, EventBridge, or another Lambda automatically. Separate success and failure destinations. Better than manual error handling for async workflows.

# Django in Lambda - anihpj example

# 1. Install Django in Lambda Layer
# pip install Django psycopg2-binary -t python/

# 2. Lambda function with Django ORM
import os
import django
from django.conf import settings

# Configure Django settings
os.environ.setdefault('DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE', 'anihpj.settings')
settings.configure(
    DATABASES={
        'default': {
            'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
            'NAME': os.environ['DB_NAME'],
            'USER': os.environ['DB_USER'],
            'PASSWORD': os.environ['DB_PASSWORD'],
            'HOST': os.environ['DB_HOST'],
            'PORT': '5432',
        }
    },
    INSTALLED_APPS=['jobpost'],
)
django.setup()

# 3. Use Django models in Lambda
from jobpost.models import JobPost, Skills

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Query using Django ORM
    python_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
        skills__name='Python',
        is_active=True
    ).select_related('location', 'author')
    
    results = [
        {
            'id': job.id,
            'title': job.title,
            'company': job.company,
            'location': str(job.location),
        }
        for job in python_jobs[:10]
    ]
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': json.dumps(results)}

✨ Best Practices

🔒 Security Checklist
Lambda Security Best Practices:

✅ IAM & Access Control
   • Principle of least privilege for execution roles
   • Use resource-based policies for cross-account access
   • Enable MFA for sensitive operations
   • Regular IAM policy audits

✅ Secrets Management
   • NEVER hardcode credentials in code
   • Use AWS Secrets Manager or Parameter Store
   • Rotate secrets regularly (automated)
   • Environment variables encrypted at rest

✅ Network Security
   • VPC for private resource access
   • Security groups with minimal ports
   • Use VPC Endpoints (avoid public internet)
   • Enable VPC Flow Logs

✅ Code Security
   • Input validation (prevent injection attacks)
   • Output encoding (prevent XSS)
   • Dependency scanning (npm audit, safety)
   • Regular security updates

✅ Monitoring & Audit
   • Enable CloudTrail for audit logs
   • CloudWatch Logs for function execution
   • Set up alarms for anomalies
   • Regular security reviews
💻 Code Best Practices
# Lambda Code Best Practices

# ✅ GOOD: Separate handler from business logic
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    """Handler delegates to business logic"""
    try:
        result = process_job_application(event)
        return success_response(result)
    except Exception as e:
        logger.error(f"Error: {str(e)}")
        return error_response(str(e))

def process_job_application(event):
    """Pure business logic - easy to test"""
    job_data = parse_event(event)
    validate_job_data(job_data)
    save_to_database(job_data)
    return {'job_id': job_data['id']}

# ✅ GOOD: Use structured logging
import logging
import json

logger = logging.getLogger()
logger.setLevel(logging.INFO)

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    logger.info(json.dumps({
        'event': 'job_created',
        'job_id': event['job_id'],
        'user_id': event['user_id'],
        'timestamp': datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
    }))

# ✅ GOOD: Implement idempotency
import hashlib

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Generate idempotency key
    event_hash = hashlib.md5(json.dumps(event, sort_keys=True).encode()).hexdigest()
    
    # Check if already processed
    if check_processed(event_hash):
        return cached_response(event_hash)
    
    result = process_event(event)
    cache_result(event_hash, result)
    return result

# ✅ GOOD: Graceful error handling
def lambda_handler(event, context):
    try:
        return process_request(event)
    except ValidationError as e:
        return {
            'statusCode': 400,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': 'Invalid input', 'details': str(e)})
        }
    except DatabaseError as e:
        logger.error(f"DB Error: {str(e)}")
        return {
            'statusCode': 500,
            'body': json.dumps({'error': 'Internal server error'})
        }
    except Exception as e:
        logger.critical(f"Unexpected error: {str(e)}")
        raise  # Let Lambda retry
