Monitoring Strategy for anihpj Lambda:

CloudWatch Metrics:
• Invocations: Total function executions
• Duration: Average, Min, Max execution time
• Errors: Failed invocations
• Throttles: Concurrent execution limit reached
• ConcurrentExecutions: Active instances

CloudWatch Alarms:
✓ Error rate > 1% → Alert via SNS
✓ Duration > 10s → Performance degradation
✓ Throttles > 0 → Need concurrency increase
✓ Cost > $100/day → Budget alert

X-Ray Tracing:
✓ End-to-end request tracing
✓ Identify bottlenecks

⚠️ Error Handling
# Comprehensive Error Handling

class LambdaError(Exception):
    """Base exception for Lambda functions"""
    pass

class RetryableError(LambdaError):
    """Error that should trigger retry"""
    pass

class NonRetryableError(LambdaError):
    """Error that should not retry"""
    pass

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    try:
        return process_event(event)
    
    except RetryableError as e:
        # Let Lambda retry automatically
        logger.warning(f"Retryable error: {str(e)}")
        raise
    
    except NonRetryableError as e:
        # Don't retry, send to DLQ
        logger.error(f"Non-retryable error: {str(e)}")
        send_to_dlq(event, str(e))
        return {'statusCode': 400, 'error': str(e)}
    
    except Exception as e:
        # Unknown error - log and retry
        logger.critical(f"Unexpected error: {str(e)}", exc_info=True)
        raise

# Configure Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)
# AWS Console → Lambda → Configuration → Asynchronous invocation
# Set DLQ: SQS queue or SNS topic for failed events

🔧 Troubleshooting

⚠️ Common Issues
1. Timeout Errors
   Symptom: "Task timed out after X seconds"
   Solutions:
   ✓ Increase timeout (max 15 minutes)
   ✓ Optimize code (reduce execution time)
   ✓ Use asynchronous processing
   ✓ Break into smaller functions

2. Out of Memory
   Symptom: "Process exited before completing request"
   Solutions:
   ✓ Increase memory allocation
   ✓ Process data in batches
   ✓ Use generators instead of lists
   ✓ Monitor memory usage with CloudWatch

3. Cold Start Latency
   Symptom: First request slow (>2 seconds)
   Solutions:
   ✓ Use Provisioned Concurrency
   ✓ Reduce package size
   ✓ Keep functions warm (scheduled pings)
   ✓ Initialize outside handler

4. VPC Connectivity Issues
   Symptom: Can't connect to RDS or internet
   Solutions:
   ✓ Check security group rules
   ✓ Verify subnet configuration
   ✓ Add NAT Gateway for internet
   ✓ Use VPC Endpoints for AWS services

5. Permission Errors
   Symptom: "AccessDeniedException"
   Solutions:
   ✓ Check IAM execution role
   ✓ Verify resource policies
   ✓ Review CloudTrail logs
   ✓ Test with elevated permissions first

❓ Frequently Asked Questions
Q: Can I run Django admin in Lambda?
A: Not recommended. Django admin requires persistent server. Use EC2 or ECS for admin interface. Lambda for APIs and background tasks only.

Q: How do I handle database connections?
A: Use connection pooling, initialize outside handler, use RDS Proxy for better connection management.

Q: What's the max execution time?
A: 15 minutes. For longer tasks, use Step Functions to chain multiple Lambdas.

Q: How many concurrent executions can I have?
A: Default 1000 per region (soft limit). Request increase via AWS Support if needed.

Q: Can Lambda access my VPC resources?
A: Yes, configure VPC, subnets, and security groups in Lambda settings.

Q: How do I deploy Lambda functions?
A: AWS Console, AWS CLI, AWS SAM, Serverless Framework, Terraform, CloudFormation.

Q: Can I use custom Python packages?
A: Yes, include in deployment package or use Lambda Layers. Binary dependencies may need special builds for Amazon Linux 2.

Q: How do I reduce cold starts?
A: Provisioned Concurrency, smaller packages, Graviton2, keep warm with scheduled pings.

⌨️ API & CLI Reference

🖥️ AWS CLI Commands
# Create Lambda function
aws lambda create-function \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
    --runtime python3.12 \
    --role arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/lambda-execution-role \
    --handler lambda_function.lambda_handler \
    --zip-file fileb://function.zip \
    --environment Variables="{DB_HOST=anihpj-db.amazonaws.com,DB_NAME=anihpj}"

# Invoke function
aws lambda invoke \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
    --payload '{"job_id": 123, "email": "user@example.com"}' \
    response.json

# Update function code
aws lambda update-function-code \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
    --zip-file fileb://new-version.zip

# Get function configuration
aws lambda get-function-configuration \
    --function-name anihpj-job-notifier

# List functions
aws lambda list-functions

# View CloudWatch logs
aws logs tail /aws/lambda/anihpj-job-notifier --follow
🐍 Boto3 SDK (Python)
import boto3
import json

lambda_client = boto3.client('lambda')

# Invoke Lambda function synchronously
response = lambda_client.invoke(
    FunctionName='anihpj-job-notifier',
    InvocationType='RequestResponse',
    Payload=json.dumps({
        'job_id': 123,
        'subscriber_email': 'user@example.com'
    })
)

result = json.loads(response['Payload'].read())
print(result)

# Invoke asynchronously (fire-and-forget)
lambda_client.invoke(
    FunctionName='anihpj-job-notifier',
    InvocationType='Event',
    Payload=json.dumps({'job_id': 456})
)

# Create function
lambda_client.create_function(
    FunctionName='anihpj-new-function',
    Runtime='python3.12',
    Role='arn:aws:iam::123:role/lambda-role',
    Handler='lambda_function.lambda_handler',
    Code={'ZipFile': open('function.zip', 'rb').read()},
    Environment={'Variables': {'DB_HOST': 'localhost'}}
)

Use Cases:
• Resume upload → Parse & extract text
• Image upload → Create thumbnails
• CSV upload → Process & import data

Configuration:
S3 Bucket → Properties → Event notifications → Add Lambda trigger
📨 SQS Queues
SQS → Lambda (Event Source Mapping)

Benefits:
• Batch processing (1-10 messages per invocation)
• Automatic retries
• Dead Letter Queue for failed messages
• Throttle protection

Configuration:
Lambda → Add trigger → SQS → Select queue
Batch size: 10
Batch window: 5 seconds

Use Case: Email notification queue
100 messages → Lambda processes in 10 batches of 10

🚚 Deployment & CI/CD

📦 Deployment Methods
Deployment Options:

1. AWS Console (Manual)
   ✓ Quick testing
   ✗ Not for production

2. AWS CLI (Scripted)
   ✓ Automation-friendly
   ✓ CI/CD integration

3. AWS SAM (Serverless Application Model)
   ✓ Infrastructure as Code
   ✓ Local testing
   ✓ API Gateway + Lambda together

4. Serverless Framework
   ✓ Multi-cloud support
   ✓ Plugin ecosystem
   ✓ Easy configuration

5. Terraform
   ✓ Infrastructure as Code
   ✓ State management
   ✓ Multi-service orchestration

6. AWS CDK (Cloud Development Kit)
   ✓ Programming language (Python, TypeScript)
   ✓ Type safety
   ✓ Reusable constructs
🔄 CI/CD Pipelines
# GitHub Actions example
name: Deploy Lambda

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
      - name: Setup Python
        uses: actions/setup-python@v4
        with:
          python-version: '3.12'
      
      - name: Install dependencies
        run: |
          pip install -r requirements.txt -t package/
          cp lambda_function.py package/
          cd package && zip -r ../function.zip .
      
      - name: Deploy to Lambda
        env:
          AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
          AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        run: |
          aws lambda update-function-code \
            --function-name anihpj-job-notifier \
            --zip-file fileb://function.zip \
            --region us-east-1

📖 Glossary

Key AWS Lambda Terms:

Cold Start
    Initial startup time when Lambda creates a new execution environment.
    Includes downloading code, starting runtime, and running init code.

Concurrency
    Number of function instances processing events simultaneously.
    Default limit: 1000 per region (can be increased).

Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)
    SQS queue or SNS topic for failed asynchronous invocations.
    Used for debugging and reprocessing failed events.

Destination
    Target service (SQS, SNS, EventBridge, Lambda) for function results.
    Separate destinations for success and failure outcomes.

Event Source
    AWS service or application that triggers Lambda function execution.
    Examples: S3, API Gateway, DynamoDB, SQS, EventBridge.

Event Source Mapping
    Configuration that reads from streams/queues and invokes Lambda.
    Used for Kinesis, DynamoDB Streams, SQS, Kafka.

Execution Environment
    Secure, isolated runtime where Lambda function code executes.
    Reused across invocations for performance (warm starts).

Execution Role
    IAM role that grants Lambda permission to access AWS services.
    Required for all Lambda functions.

Function
    Serverless application component containing code and configuration.
    Basic unit of deployment and scaling in Lambda.

Handler
    Entry point method that Lambda calls to execute your code.
    Format: filename.method_name (e.g., lambda_function.lambda_handler)

Invocation
    Single execution of a Lambda function in response to an event.
    Charged per invocation and compute time.

Lambda Layer
    ZIP archive containing libraries, dependencies, or custom runtimes.
    Shared across multiple functions to reduce package size.

Provisioned Concurrency
    Pre-initialized execution environments that eliminate cold starts.
    Additional cost but provides consistent low latency.

Reserved Concurrency
    Maximum number of concurrent instances for a specific function.
    Guarantees capacity and prevents function from consuming all account concurrency.

Runtime
    Language-specific environment for executing Lambda functions.
    Examples: Python 3.12, Node.js 20.x, Java 17, .NET 8, Go 1.x

Timeout
    Maximum time a function can run before Lambda terminates it.
    Range: 1 second to 15 minutes (900 seconds).

Trigger
    Resource or configuration that invokes Lambda function automatically.
    Examples: S3 bucket, API Gateway endpoint, CloudWatch Events rule.

Warm Start
    Fast execution when Lambda reuses existing execution environment.
    No cold start overhead, typically <10ms initialization.

X-Ray
    AWS service for tracing and analyzing Lambda function performance.
    Provides insights into execution time, downstream calls, and bottlenecks.

2024-2025
─────────
• November 2024: Python 3.13 runtime support
• October 2024: Increased ephemeral storage up to 10 GB

• January 2024: Init phase billing changes

────

• Q4: Node.js 20.x runtime support
• Q3: Recursive loop detection and protection

Key Feature Milestones:
• 2025: Multi-region active-active deployments
• 2024: Cold start optimizations (50% reduction)
• 2023: SnapStart (near-zero cold starts for Java)
• 2022: Function URLs (native HTTP endpoints)
• 2021: Container image support (up to 10 GB)
• 2020: Provisioned Concurrency (predictable performance)
• 2019: Destinations (automatic result routing)
• 2018: Lambda Layers (shared dependencies)
• 2017: Environment variables, VPC improvements
• 2016: Dead Letter Queues, versioning & aliases
• 2015: Scheduled events (cron jobs)
• 2014: AWS Lambda launched (Node.js only)

For anihpj Job Portal:
• Recommended: Use Python 3.12 runtime (latest stable)
• Architecture: ARM64 (Graviton2/3) for 20% cost savings
• Features: Use Layers for Django dependencies
• Monitoring: Enable X-Ray tracing and CloudWatch Logs Insights
• Cold Starts: Consider Provisioned Concurrency for critical APIs
• Updates: Stay on supported runtimes (AWS deprecates old versions)

⚖️ When to Use Lambda vs EC2 for anihpj

📊 Decision Matrix
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│            LAMBDA vs EC2 FOR ANIHPJ JOB PORTAL                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  USE LAMBDA FOR:                                               │
│  ✅ Background Tasks                                            │
│     • Send email notifications (new job posts)                 │
│     • Process resume uploads (PDF → text extraction)           │
│     • Generate daily/weekly reports                            │
│     • Cleanup expired job posts (scheduled)                    │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ REST API Endpoints (with API Gateway)                       │
│     • Job search API (GET /api/jobs?skills=python)            │
│     • Job details API (GET /api/jobs/{id})                     │
│     • Application submission (POST /api/jobs/{id}/apply)       │
│     • User profile updates                                     │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Event-Driven Processing                                     │
│     • S3 file upload → Process company logo                    │
│     • DynamoDB change → Update search index                    │
│     • SQS queue → Batch email sending                          │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Scheduled Tasks (Cron Jobs)                                 │
│     • Daily: Close expired job posts                           │
│     • Weekly: Send digest emails to subscribers                │
│     • Hourly: Refresh job recommendations                      │
│     • Monthly: Generate analytics reports                      │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Microservices Architecture                                  │
│     • Independent scaling per service                          │
│     • Pay only for actual usage                                │
│     • Rapid deployment and updates                             │
│                                                                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  USE EC2 FOR:                                                  │
│  ✅ Main Django Web Application                                 │
│     • Django admin interface                                   │
│     • Complex page rendering (Jinja/Django templates)          │
│     • Session management                                       │
│     • WebSocket connections (real-time features)               │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Long-Running Processes                                      │
│     • Celery workers (> 15 minutes)                            │
│     • Database migrations                                      │
│     • Large batch jobs                                         │
│     • Real-time data streaming                                 │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Stateful Applications                                       │
│     • User sessions in memory                                  │
│     • Caching layers (Redis on EC2)                            │
│     • File system dependencies                                 │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Consistent Traffic Patterns                                 │
│     • 24/7 availability required                               │
│     • Predictable baseline load                                │
│     • Reserved capacity cost savings                           │
│                                                                 │
│  ✅ Complex Dependencies                                        │
│     • Custom system libraries                                  │
│     • GPU requirements                                         │
│     • Large ML models (> 10 GB)                                │
│                                                                 │
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                 │
│  HYBRID APPROACH (RECOMMENDED FOR ANIHPJ):                     │
│                                                                 │
│  EC2: Main Django App + Database                               │
│   └─ Handles web requests, admin, complex business logic      │
│                                                                 │
│  Lambda: Event-Driven + APIs + Background Jobs                 │
│   ├─ API Gateway → Lambda (REST API for mobile apps)          │
│   ├─ S3 Trigger → Lambda (process uploaded files)             │
│   ├─ EventBridge → Lambda (scheduled cleanup tasks)           │
│   └─ SQS → Lambda (email notifications queue)                 │
│                                                                 │
│  Benefits:                                                     │
│   • Best of both worlds                                        │
│   • Cost optimization (pay-per-use for spiky workloads)       │
│   • Better scalability                                         │
│   • Reduced EC2 load                                           │
│   • Fault isolation                                            │
│                                                                 │
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Cost Comparison Example:

Scenario: anihpj with 100,000 monthly active users

EC2 ONLY:
─────────
• t3.medium (2 vCPU, 4 GB): $30/month
• m5.large for peak hours: $70/month
• Total: ~$100/month (always running)

LAMBDA ONLY (API Backend):
──────────────────────────
• 5M API requests/month
• 300ms avg, 512 MB memory
• Request charges: $0.80
• Compute charges: $24.17
• Total: ~$25/month (pay-per-use)

HYBRID (RECOMMENDED):
────────────────────
• EC2 t3.small: $15/month (main app, reduced load)
• Lambda: $20/month (APIs, background tasks)
• Total: ~$35/month + better scalability

Winner: Hybrid approach saves 65% vs EC2-only!

AWS Elastic Beanstalk

Category: Compute  |  Use Case: Managed Web Application Deployment  |  Pricing: No Additional Charge (Pay for AWS Resources)  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS Elastic Beanstalk Docs

Easy-to-use service for deploying and scaling web applications. Simply upload your Django code and Elastic Beanstalk automatically handles deployment, capacity provisioning, load balancing, and auto-scaling.

📋 Overview & Introduction

AWS Elastic Beanstalk is a Platform as a Service (PaaS) offering that simplifies deploying, managing, and scaling web applications. It abstracts away infrastructure management while still giving you full control when needed.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Quick Deployment: Deploy Django applications in minutes without infrastructure management
  • Automatic Scaling: Built-in auto-scaling based on your application's needs
  • Managed Updates: Automatic platform updates and patches
  • Full Control: Access to underlying resources (EC2, RDS, Load Balancers) when needed
  • Zero Additional Cost: Pay only for AWS resources (EC2, RDS, etc.), no Beanstalk fee
  • Multiple Environments: Easily manage dev, staging, and production environments
  • Integrated Monitoring: Built-in health monitoring and CloudWatch integration
💡 When to Use Elastic Beanstalk: Perfect for your anihpj Django job portal when you want fast deployment without managing servers, automatic scaling for traffic spikes during job postings, and easy environment management (dev/staging/production). Ideal for teams that want to focus on application code rather than infrastructure.
⚖️ Elastic Beanstalk vs. Other Compute Services
Service Control Level Management Best For anihpj Use Case
Elastic Beanstalk Medium (Managed PaaS) AWS manages infrastructure Web apps, APIs Quick Django deployment with auto-scaling
EC2 High (Full Control) You manage everything Custom configurations Custom server setup, WebSockets, background jobs
Lambda Low (Serverless) AWS manages all infrastructure Event-driven, short tasks Job notification triggers, image processing
Fargate Medium (Serverless containers) AWS manages servers Containerized microservices Docker-based Django deployment
🏗️ Elastic Beanstalk Architecture for Django
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                       AWS ELASTIC BEANSTALK ENVIRONMENT                 │
│                         (anihpj-jobportal-prod)                        │
│                                                                         │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │                    Elastic Load Balancer                          │  │
│  │              (Auto-created by Beanstalk)                          │  │

│                           │                 │                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────▼────┐  ┌─────────▼──────────────────────┐  │
│  │   EC2 Instance (AZ-1)       │  │   EC2 Instance (AZ-2)          │  │
│  │   ┌─────────────────────┐   │  │   ┌─────────────────────┐      │  │
│  │   │  Django + Gunicorn  │   │  │   │  Django + Gunicorn  │      │  │
│  │   │  anihpj JobPost     │   │  │   │  anihpj JobPost     │      │  │
│  │   └─────────────────────┘   │  │   └─────────────────────┘      │  │
│  └─────────────────────────────┘  └────────────────────────────────┘  │
│                                                                         │
│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │                    Auto Scaling Group                             │  │
│  │  • Min: 2  • Max: 10  • CPU-based scaling                        │  │
│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                                    │
                        ┌───────────▼───────────────┐
                        │   RDS PostgreSQL          │
                        │   (anihpj-jobportal-db)   │
                        └───────────────────────────┘

🔧 Core Concepts

1. Application

A logical collection of Elastic Beanstalk components (environments, versions, configurations).

eb init anihpj-jobportal --platform python-3.11
2. Environment

A version of your application running on AWS resources. Each environment has its own URL and configuration.

  • Web Server Environment: Handles HTTP requests (Django app)
  • Worker Environment: Processes background tasks from SQS
3. Platform

Combination of OS, runtime, web server, and application server. For anihpj: Python 3.11 on Amazon Linux 2023.

4. Configuration (.ebextensions)

YAML files to customize environment settings:

# .ebextensions/django.config
option_settings:
  aws:elasticbeanstalk:container:python:
    WSGIPath: "anihpj.wsgi:application"
  aws:autoscaling:asg:
    MinSize: 2
    MaxSize: 10

🚀 Getting Started with Elastic Beanstalk for Django

Step 1: Install EB CLI
pip install awsebcli
eb --version
Step 2: Initialize Application
cd /path/to/anihpj
eb init -p python-3.11 anihpj-jobportal --region us-east-1
Step 3: Configure Django Settings
# settings.py
import os

ALLOWED_HOSTS = ['.elasticbeanstalk.com', 'anihpj.com']

if 'RDS_HOSTNAME' in os.environ:
    DATABASES = {
        'default': {
            'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
            'NAME': os.environ['RDS_DB_NAME'],
            'USER': os.environ['RDS_USERNAME'],
            'PASSWORD': os.environ['RDS_PASSWORD'],
            'HOST': os.environ['RDS_HOSTNAME'],
            'PORT': os.environ['RDS_PORT'],
        }
    }
Step 4: Create Environment
eb create anihpj-prod \
    --instance-type t3.small \
    --scale 2 \
    --database \
    --database.engine postgres
Step 5: Deploy Application
eb deploy
eb open  # Opens in browser

🔑 Key Features & Components

1. Automatic Load Balancing

Distributes traffic across EC2 instances with health checks.

2. Auto Scaling

Automatically adjusts instance count based on CPU, memory, or request metrics.

3. Deployment Policies
Policy Downtime Speed Best For
All at Once Yes ⚡ Fastest Dev environments
Rolling No ⏱️ Medium Small apps
Immutable No 🐌 Slow Critical production
Blue-Green No ⏱️ Medium Zero-downtime
4. Managed Platform Updates

Automatic security patches and platform updates during maintenance windows.

5. Environment Health Monitoring

Real-time dashboard showing application health status (Green/Yellow/Red).

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

🎯 Key Point: Elastic Beanstalk is FREE. You only pay for underlying AWS resources (EC2, RDS, S3, Load Balancer).
🎯 Key Point

Elastic Beanstalk is FREE. You only pay for underlying AWS resources (EC2, RDS, S3, Load Balancer).

Typical anihpj Cost Breakdown
Resource Configuration Monthly Cost
EC2 Instances 2x t3.small $30
Load Balancer Application LB $20
RDS PostgreSQL db.t3.micro $15
S3 Storage 100GB media $2
Data Transfer 100GB out $10
Total ~$77/month
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  • Right-size instances: Start with t3.micro, scale as needed
  • Time-based scaling: Scale down during off-peak hours (nights/weekends)
  • Terminate dev environments: When not in use
  • Use S3 + CloudFront: For static files (cheaper than EC2 storage)
  • Reserved Instances: For predictable production workloads (save up to 72%)

📈 Scalability & High Availability

Auto Scaling Configuration
# .ebextensions/autoscaling.config
option_settings:
  aws:autoscaling:asg:
    MinSize: 2
    MaxSize: 10
  aws:autoscaling:trigger:
    MeasureName: CPUUtilization
    UpperThreshold: 75
    LowerThreshold: 25
Multi-AZ Deployment

Deploy across multiple availability zones for 99.95% uptime:

  • ✅ Instances distributed across 2-3 AZs
  • ✅ Multi-AZ RDS for database high availability
  • ✅ Load balancer automatically routes traffic
  • ✅ Automatic failover within 60-120 seconds

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

🎯 Quick Troubleshooting Guide for anihpj Django Deployment
Common Deployment Issues
  • 502 Bad Gateway: Check WSGI path, verify app is running on port 8000
  • Health Check Failures: Ensure /health/ endpoint returns HTTP 200
  • Static Files 404: Run collectstatic, configure proxy settings
  • Database Connection: Verify RDS security group allows EC2 access
  • Deployment Timeout: Check container_commands, migrations may be too slow

🚀 Deployment & CI/CD

Automated Deployment Pipeline
GitHub Actions CI/CD for anihpj:
# .github/workflows/deploy.yml
name: Deploy to Elastic Beanstalk

on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Generate deployment package
      run: zip -r deploy.zip . -x '*.git*'
    
    - name: Deploy to EB
      uses: einaregilsson/beanstalk-deploy@v21
      with:
        aws_access_key: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        aws_secret_key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        application_name: anihpj-jobportal
        environment_name: anihpj-prod
        version_label: ${{ github.sha }}
        region: us-east-1
        deployment_package: deploy.zip

🛡️ Compliance & Governance

Security & Compliance
  • Certifications: SOC, PCI DSS, HIPAA, ISO 27001 (inherited from AWS services)
  • Encryption: At-rest (EBS, RDS, S3) and in-transit (TLS/SSL)
  • IAM Roles: Use instance profiles for secure AWS service access
  • VPC: Deploy in private subnets with NAT gateway
  • Monitoring: CloudWatch Logs, CloudTrail for audit trails
✅ anihpj Production Checklist:
  • ✅ HTTPS enforced with ACM certificate
  • ✅ Secrets in AWS Secrets Manager
  • ✅ Multi-AZ deployment (HA)
  • ✅ Automated backups (RDS 7-day retention)
  • ✅ CloudWatch monitoring + alarms
  • ✅ Security groups properly configured
  • ✅ IAM roles with least-privilege access
🎉 AWS Elastic Beanstalk Summary

Elastic Beanstalk is the fastest way to deploy your anihpj Django job portal to AWS. With zero additional cost, automatic scaling, and managed updates, you can focus on building features while AWS handles the infrastructure.

Perfect for: Django web apps, REST APIs, quick deployments, development teams focused on application code.

Cost: ~$70-150/month for production-ready setup with HA.

📖 Glossary

Term Definition
Application Logical collection of Elastic Beanstalk components (environments, versions, configurations). For anihpj: "anihpj-jobportal"
Environment Collection of AWS resources running an application version. Examples: anihpj-dev, anihpj-staging, anihpj-prod
Environment Tier Web Server (HTTP traffic) or Worker (background jobs from SQS)
Platform Combination of OS, runtime, web server, and application server. E.g., "Python 3.11 running on 64bit Amazon Linux 2023"
Application Version Specific, labeled iteration of deployable code for an application. E.g., "v1.5.0-job-search-feature"
.ebextensions Directory containing YAML files to customize environment configuration and resources
.platform Directory for advanced platform customization using hooks and scripts
EB CLI Command-line interface for creating, managing, and deploying Beanstalk applications
Blue-Green Deployment Deployment strategy using two identical environments to enable zero-downtime updates
Immutable Deployment Deployment that launches new instances with new code before terminating old ones
Rolling Deployment Deployment that updates instances in batches to maintain availability
Saved Configuration Template for environment settings that can be reused across environments
Health Reporting Enhanced monitoring showing application health based on metrics and health checks
Managed Updates Automatic platform updates during maintenance windows
WSGI Web Server Gateway Interface - Standard interface for Python web applications. Django uses: anihpj.wsgi:application

⚔️ Elastic Beanstalk vs. EC2 vs. Lambda vs. Fargate

Detailed Service Comparison for anihpj Django Deployment
Feature Elastic Beanstalk EC2 Lambda Fargate
Management Level Managed PaaS Infrastructure (IaaS) Serverless (FaaS) Serverless Containers
Control ⭐⭐⭐ Medium ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Full ⭐ Limited ⭐⭐⭐ Medium
Setup Time ⚡ 5-10 minutes 🐌 30-60 minutes ⚡⚡ 2-5 minutes ⚡ 10-15 minutes
Scaling Automatic (CPU-based) Manual or Auto Scaling Group Automatic (instant) Automatic (container-based)
Pricing Model Free (pay for resources) Hourly instance charges Per-request + duration Per-second (vCPU + memory)
anihpj Cost 💰 $70-150/month 💰💰 $100-200/month 💰 $10-50/month 💰 $80-180/month
Load Balancing ✅ Built-in (auto-created) Manual setup required ✅ API Gateway ✅ ALB/NLB integration
Health Monitoring ✅ Enhanced built-in CloudWatch only ✅ CloudWatch Logs ✅ Container Insights
Deployment eb deploy (1 command) Custom scripts/tools SAM/Serverless/CDK ECS/Docker push
Multi-Environment ✅ Easy (dev/staging/prod) Manual setup ✅ Stages/Aliases ✅ ECS Services
Database Integration ✅ RDS auto-config Manual configuration ⚠️ Connection pooling issues Manual configuration
WebSockets ✅ Supported ✅ Full support ✅ API Gateway (limited) ✅ Full support
Long-Running Tasks ✅ Worker tier ✅ Unlimited ❌ 15 min max ✅ Unlimited
Custom Software ⚠️ Limited (.ebextensions) ✅ Full control ❌ Runtime only ✅ Docker images
Maintenance Effort ⭐ Low (AWS manages) ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ High ⭐ Very Low ⭐⭐ Low-Medium
🎯 When to Choose Each Service for anihpj
Choose Elastic Beanstalk when:
  • ✅ You want fast deployment without managing infrastructure
  • ✅ You need automatic scaling for traffic spikes (job posting deadlines)
  • ✅ You want easy multi-environment management (dev/staging/prod)
  • ✅ Your team focuses on Django code, not DevOps
  • ✅ You need traditional web app architecture with persistent connections
Choose EC2 when:
  • ✅ You need full control over server configuration
  • ✅ You have custom software requirements (specific OS, system packages)
  • ✅ You need WebSocket connections for real-time job alerts
  • ✅ You want to run background workers alongside web servers
  • ✅ Cost optimization through Reserved Instances for predictable load
Choose Lambda when:
  • ✅ Building event-driven features (job notification triggers)
  • ✅ Image processing for resume uploads
  • ✅ Scheduled tasks (daily job expiration checks)
  • ✅ API endpoints with sporadic traffic
  • ✅ You want to pay only for actual execution time
Choose Fargate when:
  • ✅ You prefer Docker-based deployments
  • ✅ You need microservices architecture
  • ✅ You want serverless but with containers
  • ✅ You need precise resource control (vCPU/memory)
  • ✅ You have existing Docker workflows
💡 Hybrid Approach for anihpj (Recommended)

🎓 Final Recommendation for anihpj:

Start with Elastic Beanstalk for the main Django application. It provides the best balance of simplicity, features, and cost for a job portal. As your application grows, add Lambda functions for specific event-driven tasks and consider EC2 for specialized workloads that need custom configuration.

Migration Path: Beanstalk (MVP) → Beanstalk + Lambda (Scale) → Beanstalk + Lambda + EC2 Workers (Enterprise)

AWS Fargate

Category: Compute  |  Use Case: Serverless Container Orchestration  |  Pricing: Per-Second vCPU and Memory  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS Fargate Docs

Serverless compute engine for containers that works with Amazon ECS and EKS. Deploy and manage containers without managing servers or clusters, paying only for the resources your containerized applications use.

📋 Overview & Introduction

AWS Fargate is a serverless compute engine for containers that removes the need to provision and manage servers. You define your application's requirements (CPU, memory, networking) and Fargate launches and scales the compute, allowing you to focus on building applications rather than managing infrastructure.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Serverless: No servers to provision, patch, or scale
  • Container-Native: Deploy Docker containers with full isolation
  • Pay-per-Use: Pay only for vCPU and memory resources consumed per second
  • Scalable: Automatically scales with application demand
  • Secure: Task-level isolation with AWS IAM and VPC networking
  • Integrated: Works seamlessly with ECS and EKS
  • Flexible: Support for various compute configurations
💡 When to Use Fargate: Perfect for your anihpj Django job portal when you want containerized deployments without managing EC2 instances, microservices architecture, or batch processing jobs. Ideal for teams familiar with Docker who want the benefits of containers without infrastructure overhead.
⚖️ Fargate vs. Other Compute Services
Service Management Best For anihpj Use Case
Fargate Serverless containers Containerized apps, microservices Docker-based Django with auto-scaling
ECS on EC2 Container orchestration on EC2 Custom instance requirements Cost optimization with Reserved Instances
EKS Managed Kubernetes Complex orchestration needs Advanced microservices with Kubernetes
Lambda Serverless functions Event-driven, short tasks Job notification triggers
EC2 Full server control Custom configurations Traditional deployment with full access
🏗️ Fargate Architecture for Django
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

                                    │
                        ┌───────────▼───────────────┐
                        │   RDS PostgreSQL          │
                        │   (anihpj-jobportal-db)   │
                        └───────────────────────────┘

🔧 Core Concepts

1. Task Definition

Blueprint for your application that specifies containers, CPU, memory, networking, and IAM roles. Like a Dockerfile configuration but for AWS.

{
  "family": "anihpj-django-task",
  "networkMode": "awsvpc",
  "requiresCompatibilities": ["FARGATE"],
  "cpu": "512",
  "memory": "1024",
  "containerDefinitions": [{
    "name": "anihpj-web",
    "image": "123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest",
    "portMappings": [{"containerPort": 8000, "protocol": "tcp"}],
    "environment": [
      {"name": "DEBUG", "value": "False"},
      {"name": "DATABASE_URL", "value": "postgresql://..."}
    ]
  }]
}
2. Service

Manages and maintains the desired number of task instances. Ensures tasks are running and integrates with load balancers.

3. Cluster

Logical grouping of tasks or services. With Fargate, you don't manage the underlying infrastructure.

4. Task vs Task Definition
  • Task Definition: Template (blueprint)
  • Task: Running instance of a task definition
  • Think: Class (Task Definition) vs Object (Task)

🚀 Getting Started with Fargate for Django

Step 1: Create Dockerfile for anihpj
# Dockerfile
FROM python:3.11-slim

WORKDIR /app

# Install dependencies
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt
RUN pip install gunicorn psycopg2-binary

# Copy application
COPY . .

# Collect static files
RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Expose port
EXPOSE 8000

# Run application
CMD ["gunicorn", "anihpj.wsgi:application", "--bind", "0.0.0.0:8000", "--workers", "3"]
Step 2: Build and Push to ECR
# Authenticate Docker to ECR
aws ecr get-login-password --region us-east-1 | docker login --username AWS --password-stdin 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com

# Create ECR repository
aws ecr create-repository --repository-name anihpj --region us-east-1

# Build Docker image
docker build -t anihpj:latest .

# Tag image
docker tag anihpj:latest 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest

# Push to ECR
docker push 123456789012.dkr.ecr.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/anihpj:latest
Step 3: Create Task Definition
# Create task-definition.json
aws ecs register-task-definition --cli-input-json file://task-definition.json
Step 4: Create ECS Cluster
aws ecs create-cluster --cluster-name anihpj-cluster --region us-east-1
Step 5: Create Service
aws ecs create-service \
    --cluster anihpj-cluster \
    --service-name anihpj-service \
    --task-definition anihpj-django-task \
    --desired-count 2 \
    --launch-type FARGATE \
    --network-configuration "awsvpcConfiguration={subnets=[subnet-12345],securityGroups=[sg-12345],assignPublicIp=ENABLED}" \
    --load-balancers "targetGroupArn=arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:...,containerName=anihpj-web,containerPort=8000"

🔑 Key Features & Components

1. Serverless Infrastructure

No EC2 instances to manage. AWS handles provisioning, scaling, and maintenance automatically.

2. Task-Level Isolation

Each task runs in its own isolated environment with dedicated kernel, CPU, memory, and network resources.

3. Right-Sizing Options
CPU (vCPU) Memory Options (GB) anihpj Recommendation
0.25 0.5, 1, 2 Development/Testing
0.5 1, 2, 3, 4 ✅ Small Production (Recommended)
1 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8 Medium Production
2 4-16 GB Large Production
4 8-30 GB High Traffic
4. AWS VPC Networking

Tasks run within your VPC with full control over security groups, subnets, and network ACLs.

5. Integrated Monitoring

CloudWatch Container Insights for metrics, logs, and traces. X-Ray for distributed tracing.

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

🎯 Fargate Pricing Model:

Pay only for vCPU and memory resources used per second (1-minute minimum). No charges for idle infrastructure.

Typical anihpj Cost Breakdown
Resource Configuration Monthly Cost
Fargate Tasks 2x (0.5 vCPU, 1GB) running 24/7 $35
Application Load Balancer Standard ALB $20
RDS PostgreSQL db.t3.micro $15
ECR Storage 5GB Docker images $0.50
Data Transfer 100GB out $10
Total ~$80/month
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  • Right-size tasks: Start small (0.25 vCPU) and scale up based on metrics
  • Use Spot capacity: Save up to 70% for fault-tolerant workloads
  • Scale to zero: For dev/test environments, scale down when not in use
  • Optimize Docker images: Smaller images = faster startup = lower costs
  • Use Savings Plans: Commit to consistent usage for 20-50% savings
  • Consolidate containers: Run multiple related containers in one task

📈 Scalability & High Availability

Auto Scaling Configuration
# Register scalable target
aws application-autoscaling register-scalable-target \
    --service-namespace ecs \
    --resource-id service/anihpj-cluster/anihpj-service \
    --scalable-dimension ecs:service:DesiredCount \
    --min-capacity 1 \
    --max-capacity 10

# Create CPU-based scaling policy
aws application-autoscaling put-scaling-policy \
    --policy-name anihpj-cpu-scaling \
    --service-namespace ecs \
    --resource-id service/anihpj-cluster/anihpj-service \
    --scalable-dimension ecs:service:DesiredCount \
    --policy-type TargetTrackingScaling \
    --target-tracking-scaling-policy-configuration file://scaling-policy.json
Multi-AZ Deployment

Best practices for high availability:

  • ✅ Deploy tasks across 2-3 availability zones
  • ✅ Use Application Load Balancer for health checks
  • ✅ Configure task placement strategies
  • ✅ Set up automatic task recovery
  • ✅ Multi-AZ RDS for database redundancy

1. Fargate Spot

Run fault-tolerant tasks at up to 70% discount:

{
  "capacityProviderStrategy": [
    {
      "capacityProvider": "FARGATE_SPOT",
      "weight": 4,
      "base": 0
    },
    {
      "capacityProvider": "FARGATE",
      "weight": 1,
      "base": 2
    }
  ]
}
2. Secrets Management

Store sensitive data securely:

"secrets": [
  {
    "name": "DATABASE_PASSWORD",
    "valueFrom": "arn:aws:secretsmanager:us-east-1:123456789012:secret:anihpj-db-password"
  },
  {
    "name": "SECRET_KEY",
    "valueFrom": "arn:aws:secretsmanager:us-east-1:123456789012:secret:anihpj-django-secret"
  }
]

"volumes": [{
  "name": "anihpj-media",

    "transitEncryption": "ENABLED"

}]
4. CI/CD with GitHub Actions
# .github/workflows/deploy-fargate.yml
name: Deploy to Fargate
on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
      - name: Configure AWS credentials
        uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v2
        with:
          aws-access-key-id: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
          aws-secret-access-key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
          aws-region: us-east-1
      
      - name: Login to Amazon ECR
        id: login-ecr
        uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecr-login@v1
      
      - name: Build and push Docker image
        env:
          ECR_REGISTRY: ${{ steps.login-ecr.outputs.registry }}
          ECR_REPOSITORY: anihpj
          IMAGE_TAG: ${{ github.sha }}
        run: |
          docker build -t $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG .
          docker push $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG
      
      - name: Update ECS service
        run: |
          aws ecs update-service \
            --cluster anihpj-cluster \
            --service anihpj-service \
            --force-new-deployment

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

🎯 Quick Troubleshooting Guide for anihpj Fargate Deployment
Common Deployment Issues
  • Task Fails to Start: Check CloudWatch logs, verify Docker image exists in ECR
  • Out of Memory: Increase memory allocation in task definition
  • Network Timeout: Verify security groups allow outbound traffic, check NAT gateway
  • Cannot Pull Image: Verify IAM role has ECR permissions
  • Health Check Failing: Ensure container exposes correct port and responds to health checks
Frequently Asked Questions
  • Q: Can I SSH into Fargate tasks?
    A: No, but you can use ECS Exec for debugging
  • Q: How do I persist data?
    A: Use EFS volumes or external databases like RDS
  • Q: What's the cold start time?
    A: Typically 30-60 seconds for task startup
  • Q: Can I use GPU?
    A: Yes, Fargate supports GPU tasks for ML workloads
  • Q: How do I debug issues?
    A: Use CloudWatch Logs, Container Insights, and AWS X-Ray

⌨️ API & CLI Quick Reference

Essential ECS/Fargate CLI Commands
# Cluster Management
aws ecs create-cluster --cluster-name anihpj-cluster
aws ecs list-clusters
aws ecs describe-clusters --clusters anihpj-cluster
aws ecs delete-cluster --cluster anihpj-cluster

# Task Definitions
aws ecs register-task-definition --cli-input-json file://task-def.json
aws ecs list-task-definitions
aws ecs describe-task-definition --task-definition anihpj-django-task
aws ecs deregister-task-definition --task-definition anihpj-django-task:1

# Services
aws ecs create-service --cli-input-json file://service.json
aws ecs list-services --cluster anihpj-cluster
aws ecs describe-services --cluster anihpj-cluster --services anihpj-service
aws ecs update-service --cluster anihpj-cluster --service anihpj-service --force-new-deployment
aws ecs delete-service --cluster anihpj-cluster --service anihpj-service

# Tasks
aws ecs list-tasks --cluster anihpj-cluster
aws ecs describe-tasks --cluster anihpj-cluster --tasks task-id
aws ecs run-task --cluster anihpj-cluster --task-definition anihpj-django-task --launch-type FARGATE
aws ecs stop-task --cluster anihpj-cluster --task task-id

# Logs
aws logs tail /ecs/anihpj-django-task --follow
aws logs get-log-events --log-group-name /ecs/anihpj-django-task --log-stream-name ecs/anihpj-web/task-id

🚀 Deployment & CI/CD

Complete GitHub Actions Workflow
# .github/workflows/deploy-to-fargate.yml
name: Deploy anihpj to AWS Fargate

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

env:
  AWS_REGION: us-east-1
  ECR_REPOSITORY: anihpj
  ECS_CLUSTER: anihpj-cluster
  ECS_SERVICE: anihpj-service
  ECS_TASK_DEFINITION: anihpj-django-task

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
    steps:
    - name: Checkout code
      uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Configure AWS credentials
      uses: aws-actions/configure-aws-credentials@v2
      with:
        aws-access-key-id: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        aws-secret-access-key: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        aws-region: ${{ env.AWS_REGION }}
    
    - name: Login to Amazon ECR
      id: login-ecr
      uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecr-login@v1
    
    - name: Build, tag, and push image to Amazon ECR
      id: build-image
      env:
        ECR_REGISTRY: ${{ steps.login-ecr.outputs.registry }}
        IMAGE_TAG: ${{ github.sha }}
      run: |
        docker build -t $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG .
        docker push $ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG
        echo "image=$ECR_REGISTRY/$ECR_REPOSITORY:$IMAGE_TAG" >> $GITHUB_OUTPUT
    
    - name: Download task definition
      run: |
        aws ecs describe-task-definition \
          --task-definition ${{ env.ECS_TASK_DEFINITION }} \
          --query taskDefinition > task-definition.json
    
    - name: Fill in the new image ID in the Amazon ECS task definition
      id: task-def
      uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecs-render-task-definition@v1
      with:
        task-definition: task-definition.json
        container-name: anihpj-web
        image: ${{ steps.build-image.outputs.image }}
    
    - name: Deploy Amazon ECS task definition
      uses: aws-actions/amazon-ecs-deploy-task-definition@v1
      with:
        task-definition: ${{ steps.task-def.outputs.task-definition }}
        service: ${{ env.ECS_SERVICE }}
        cluster: ${{ env.ECS_CLUSTER }}
        wait-for-service-stability: true

🛡️ Compliance & Governance

Security & Compliance
  • Certifications: SOC, PCI DSS, HIPAA, ISO 27001, FedRAMP
  • Task Isolation: Dedicated kernel runtime per task
  • Encryption: At-rest (EBS volumes) and in-transit (TLS)
  • IAM Integration: Fine-grained task-level permissions
  • VPC Security: Private networking with security groups
✅ anihpj Fargate Production Checklist:
  • ✅ Tasks in private subnets with NAT gateway
  • ✅ Secrets in AWS Secrets Manager
  • ✅ Multi-AZ task deployment
  • ✅ CloudWatch Container Insights enabled
  • ✅ ALB with HTTPS and ACM certificate
  • ✅ Task IAM roles with least privilege
  • ✅ Auto Scaling configured (min 2, max 10)
  • ✅ RDS automated backups enabled
  • ✅ Docker image vulnerability scanning
  • ✅ CI/CD pipeline for automated deployments

📖 Glossary

Term Definition
Task Definition Blueprint specifying containers, CPU, memory, and networking for your application
Task Running instance of a task definition (similar to EC2 instance)
Service Manages desired number of task instances and integrates with load balancers
Cluster Logical grouping of tasks and services
ECR Elastic Container Registry - AWS Docker image repository
ECS Elastic Container Service - Container orchestration service
awsvpc Network mode giving each task an elastic network interface (ENI)
Launch Type FARGATE (serverless) or EC2 (manage instances)
Capacity Provider Strategy for task placement (FARGATE, FARGATE_SPOT)
Task Role IAM role for applications running in task containers
Execution Role IAM role for ECS agent (pull images, send logs)
Container Insights CloudWatch monitoring for containerized applications
Fargate Spot Run tasks on spare Fargate capacity at up to 70% discount

🎯 When to Choose Fargate for anihpj
Choose Fargate when:
  • ✅ You want containerized Django without managing servers
  • ✅ You need microservices architecture (API + Workers + Services)
  • ✅ You prefer Docker-based deployments
  • ✅ You want pay-per-use pricing without idle costs
  • ✅ You need task-level security isolation
  • ✅ You want to avoid EC2 instance management overhead

🎓 Final Recommendation for anihpj:

Choose Fargate if you're comfortable with Docker and want the benefits of containers without managing servers. It's ideal for teams that want modern containerized deployments with microservices potential.

Cost-Benefit: Slightly higher than Beanstalk but provides better isolation, flexibility, and scalability. Perfect middle ground between serverless (Lambda) and full control (EC2).

Migration Path: Monolithic Django on Fargate (MVP) → Microservices (Scale) → Hybrid with Lambda + RDS (Enterprise)

💾 Storage Services

AWS offers various storage solutions for different use cases, from object storage to block storage and file systems.

Amazon S3 (Simple Storage Service)

Category: Storage  |  Use Case: Object Storage for Static Files, Media, Backups  |  Pricing: Pay-per-GB Stored + Data Transfer  |  Last Updated: November 2025  |  Documentation: AWS S3 Docs

Amazon S3 is an object storage service offering industry-leading scalability, data availability, security, and performance. Perfect for storing Django static files, user-uploaded media (resumes, company logos), backups, and application data.

📋 Overview & Introduction

Amazon S3 provides object storage through a web services interface. You can store and retrieve any amount of data at any time from anywhere on the web. It's designed for 99.999999999% (11 9's) durability and stores data for millions of applications.

🎯 Key Benefits
  • Durability: 99.999999999% (11 9's) object durability
  • Scalability: Store unlimited data without capacity planning
  • Availability: 99.99% availability SLA for Standard tier
  • Security: Encryption at rest and in transit, IAM policies, bucket policies
  • Performance: Automatically scales to high request rates
  • Cost-Effective: Multiple storage classes for cost optimization
  • Integration: Works seamlessly with Django, CloudFront, Lambda
💡 Perfect for anihpj: Store Django static files (CSS, JS), user-uploaded resumes, company logos, job posting attachments, database backups, and application logs. S3 is the foundation for scalable file storage in your job portal.
⚖️ S3 vs. Other Storage Services
Service Type Best For anihpj Use Case
S3 Object Storage Static files, media, backups Resumes, logos, static assets
EBS Block Storage EC2 instance volumes EC2 root volume, databases
EFS File Storage Shared file systems Shared media across multiple servers
Glacier Archive Storage Long-term archival Old job posting archives, compliance

🔧 Core Concepts

1. Buckets

Containers for storing objects. Bucket names must be globally unique across all AWS accounts.

# Create bucket for anihpj
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-static --region us-east-1
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-media --region us-east-1
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-backups --region us-east-1
2. Objects

Files stored in S3. Each object consists of data, metadata, and a unique key (filename).

  • Key: Object name/path (e.g., resumes/user_123/resume.pdf)
  • Value: The actual file data (up to 5TB per object)
  • Metadata: Key-value pairs describing the object
  • Version ID: If versioning is enabled
3. Storage Classes
Class Use Case Availability Cost
Standard Frequently accessed 99.99% $$
Standard-IA Infrequent access 99.9% $
One Zone-IA Non-critical, infrequent 99.5% $
Glacier Archive (minutes-hours) 99.99% ¢
Glacier Deep Long-term archive 99.99% ¢
4. Versioning

Keep multiple variants of an object. Protects from accidental deletions and overwrites.

5. Access Control
  • IAM Policies: User/role-based permissions
  • Bucket Policies: Resource-based permissions
  • ACLs: Legacy access control lists
  • Pre-signed URLs: Temporary access to private objects

🚀 Getting Started with S3 for Django

Step 1: Install Required Packages
# Install django-storages and boto3
pip install django-storages boto3

# Add to requirements.txt
echo "django-storages==1.14.2" >> requirements.txt
echo "boto3==1.34.18" >> requirements.txt
Step 2: Configure Django Settings
# anihpj/settings.py
import os

# Add to INSTALLED_APPS
INSTALLED_APPS = [
    # ... other apps
    'storages',
]

# AWS S3 Configuration
AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID = os.environ.get('AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID')
AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY = os.environ.get('AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY')
AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME = 'anihpj-media'
AWS_S3_REGION_NAME = 'us-east-1'
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = f'{AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME}.s3.amazonaws.com'

# Static files (CSS, JavaScript, Images)
STATICFILES_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/static/'

# Media files (User uploads)
DEFAULT_FILE_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/media/'

# Optional: Use CloudFront CDN
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = 'd1234abcd.cloudfront.net'

# S3 Settings
AWS_S3_FILE_OVERWRITE = False
AWS_DEFAULT_ACL = None
AWS_S3_VERIFY = True
Step 3: Create S3 Buckets
# Create buckets
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-static
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-media
aws s3 mb s3://anihpj-backups

# Enable versioning on media bucket
aws s3api put-bucket-versioning \
    --bucket anihpj-media \
    --versioning-configuration Status=Enabled

# Enable server-side encryption
aws s3api put-bucket-encryption \
    --bucket anihpj-media \
    --server-side-encryption-configuration '{
        "Rules": [{
            "ApplyServerSideEncryptionByDefault": {
                "SSEAlgorithm": "AES256"
            }
        }]
    }'
Step 4: Set Bucket Policy
{
  "Version": "2012-10-17",
  "Statement": [
    {
      "Sid": "PublicReadGetObject",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Principal": "*",
      "Action": "s3:GetObject",
      "Resource": "arn:aws:s3:::anihpj-static/*"
    },
    {
      "Sid": "DjangoAppUpload",
      "Effect": "Allow",
      "Principal": {
        "AWS": "arn:aws:iam::123456789012:user/anihpj-app"
      },
      "Action": [
        "s3:PutObject",
        "s3:GetObject",
        "s3:DeleteObject"
      ],
      "Resource": "arn:aws:s3:::anihpj-media/*"
    }
  ]
}
Step 5: Use S3 in Django Models
# jobpost/models.py
from django.db import models

class JobPost(models.Model):
    title = models.CharField(max_length=200)
    company_logo = models.ImageField(
        upload_to='company-logos/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )  # Auto-uploads to S3: s3://anihpj-media/company-logos/
    
    job_description_pdf = models.FileField(
        upload_to='job-attachments/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )  # Auto-uploads to S3
    
    created_at = models.DateTimeField(auto_now_add=True)

class UserProfile(models.Model):
    user = models.OneToOneField(User, on_delete=models.CASCADE)
    resume = models.FileField(
        upload_to='resumes/',
        blank=True,
        null=True
    )  # Stored in: s3://anihpj-media/resumes/resume_xyz.pdf

🔑 Key Features & Capabilities

1. Lifecycle Management

Automatically transition objects between storage classes or delete them.

{
  "Rules": [
    {
      "Id": "ArchiveOldResumes",
      "Status": "Enabled",
      "Filter": {"Prefix": "resumes/"},
      "Transitions": [
        {
          "Days": 90,
          "StorageClass": "STANDARD_IA"
        },
        {
          "Days": 365,
          "StorageClass": "GLACIER"
        }
      ]
    },
    {
      "Id": "DeleteTempFiles",
      "Status": "Enabled",
      "Filter": {"Prefix": "temp/"},
      "Expiration": {"Days": 7}
    }
  ]
}
2. Cross-Region Replication

Automatically replicate objects across AWS regions for disaster recovery.

3. Event Notifications

Trigger Lambda functions, SQS queues, or SNS topics when objects are created/deleted.

# Lambda function triggered on resume upload
import boto3

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    # Get bucket and key from S3 event
    bucket = event['Records'][0]['s3']['bucket']['name']
    key = event['Records'][0]['s3']['object']['key']
    
    # Process uploaded resume (virus scan, format validation)
    print(f"New resume uploaded: s3://{bucket}/{key}")
    
    # Send notification to recruiter
    # ...
4. Pre-signed URLs

Generate temporary URLs for secure access to private objects.

# Django view to generate download link
import boto3
from datetime import timedelta

def generate_resume_download(request, resume_id):
    s3_client = boto3.client('s3')
    
    # Generate pre-signed URL (valid for 1 hour)
    url = s3_client.generate_presigned_url(
        'get_object',
        Params={
            'Bucket': 'anihpj-media',
            'Key': f'resumes/{resume_id}.pdf'
        },
        ExpiresIn=3600  # 1 hour
    )
    
    return JsonResponse({'download_url': url})
5. Transfer Acceleration

Use CloudFront edge locations to speed up uploads by up to 50-500%.

💰 Pricing & Cost Optimization

🎯 S3 Pricing Components:
  • Storage: $0.023/GB/month (Standard, first 50TB)
  • Requests: $0.0004 per 1,000 PUT/POST, $0.0004 per 10,000 GET
  • Data Transfer: $0.09/GB out to internet (first 10TB)
  • Storage Classes: Standard-IA 50% cheaper, Glacier 90% cheaper
Typical anihpj Cost Breakdown
Component Usage Monthly Cost
Storage (Standard) 50GB static files + media $1.15
Storage (Standard-IA) 100GB backups $1.25
PUT/POST Requests 10,000 uploads/month $0.05
GET Requests 100,000 downloads/month $0.04
Data Transfer Out 20GB/month $1.80
CloudFront CDN 50GB transfer $4.25
Total ~$8.50/month
💡 Cost Optimization Tips
  • Use CloudFront: Reduces S3 data transfer costs by 70%
  • Lifecycle policies: Auto-move old files to cheaper storage
  • Intelligent-Tiering: Auto-optimize based on access patterns
  • Delete unused files: Remove temp files, old backups
  • Compress files: Gzip CSS/JS before uploading
  • Right-size images: Don't store 10MB logos when 100KB works

📈 Scalability & High Availability

Automatic Scaling
  • ✅ Scales automatically to handle any request rate
  • ✅ Supports 3,500 PUT/POST and 5,500 GET requests per second per prefix
  • ✅ No capacity planning required
  • ✅ Partition keys (prefixes) for higher throughput
Durability & Availability
  • 99.999999999% durability: Data replicated across 3+ AZs
  • 99.99% availability: Designed for Standard class
  • Cross-Region Replication: For disaster recovery
  • Versioning: Protection against accidental deletion

🎓 Advanced Topics

1. S3 + CloudFront CDN

Serve static files from edge locations for faster delivery.

# Django settings with CloudFront
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = 'd1234abcd.cloudfront.net'
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/static/'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/media/'

# CloudFront distribution settings
# - Origin: anihpj-static.s3.amazonaws.com
# - Cache behavior: Cache based on query strings
# - TTL: 1 year for static, 1 hour for media
# - SSL Certificate: ACM certificate
2. Multipart Upload

Upload large files (>100MB) in parts for better performance.

import boto3
from boto3.s3.transfer import TransferConfig

s3_client = boto3.client('s3')

# Configure multipart upload (5MB chunks)
config = TransferConfig(
    multipart_threshold=1024 * 25,  # 25MB
    max_concurrency=10,
    multipart_chunksize=1024 * 25
)

# Upload large file
s3_client.upload_file(
    'large_video.mp4',
    'anihpj-media',
    'videos/large_video.mp4',
    Config=config
)
3. Server-Side Encryption
  • SSE-S3: AWS-managed keys (AES-256)
  • SSE-KMS: AWS KMS-managed keys (audit trail)
  • SSE-C: Customer-provided keys
4. Static Website Hosting
# Enable static website hosting
aws s3 website s3://anihpj-static \
    --index-document index.html \
    --error-document error.html

# Website endpoint: http://anihpj-static.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com

✨ Best Practices

💼 Common Use Cases

Use Case 1: Django Static Files

Scenario: Serve CSS, JavaScript, and images for anihpj from S3 + CloudFront.

# Collect static files to S3
python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Files are automatically uploaded to:
# s3://anihpj-static/static/css/
# s3://anihpj-static/static/js/
# s3://anihpj-static/static/images/
Use Case 2: User-Uploaded Files

Store resumes, company logos, and job attachments with automatic S3 upload.

# View for file upload
from django.core.files.storage import default_storage

def upload_resume(request):
    if request.method == 'POST':
        resume_file = request.FILES['resume']
        
        # Automatically uploads to S3
        file_path = default_storage.save(
            f'resumes/{request.user.id}/{resume_file.name}',
            resume_file
        )
        
        # Get S3 URL
        file_url = default_storage.url(file_path)
        # Returns: https://anihpj-media.s3.amazonaws.com/resumes/123/resume.pdf
Use Case 3: Database & Application Backups
# Automated backup script
#!/bin/bash
DATE=$(date +%Y-%m-%d)

# Backup PostgreSQL database
pg_dump anihpj_db | gzip > /tmp/backup_$DATE.sql.gz

# Upload to S3
aws s3 cp /tmp/backup_$DATE.sql.gz s3://anihpj-backups/database/

# Cleanup local file
rm /tmp/backup_$DATE.sql.gz

🔧 Troubleshooting & FAQs

🎯 Quick Troubleshooting Guide for anihpj S3 Issues
Common Issues
  • 403 Forbidden: Check IAM permissions, bucket policy, and CORS configuration
  • Slow uploads: Use Transfer Acceleration or multipart uploads
  • Files not appearing: Verify bucket name, region, and AWS credentials
  • CORS errors: Configure CORS policy on S3 bucket
  • High costs: Review data transfer, implement lifecycle policies
Frequently Asked Questions
  • Q: What's the max file size?
    A: 5TB per object (use multipart upload for >5GB)
  • Q: Can I use custom domain?
    A: Yes, via CloudFront with Route 53
  • Q: How secure is S3?
    A: Very secure with encryption, IAM, VPC endpoints
  • Q: Can I host entire Django app?
    A: Only static files; use EC2/Fargate/Beanstalk for Django app
  • Q: How to prevent accidental deletion?
    A: Enable versioning + MFA Delete

⌨️ API & CLI Quick Reference

Essential S3 CLI Commands
# Bucket Operations
aws s3 mb s3://bucket-name                    # Create bucket
aws s3 ls                                     # List all buckets
aws s3 ls s3://bucket-name                    # List objects in bucket
aws s3 rb s3://bucket-name --force            # Delete bucket and contents

# File Operations
aws s3 cp file.txt s3://bucket/path/          # Upload file
aws s3 cp s3://bucket/path/file.txt .         # Download file
aws s3 sync ./local s3://bucket/path/         # Sync directory
aws s3 rm s3://bucket/path/file.txt           # Delete file
aws s3 mv s3://bucket/old.txt s3://bucket/new.txt  # Move/rename

# Recursive Operations
aws s3 cp ./static s3://bucket/static/ --recursive
aws s3 rm s3://bucket/temp/ --recursive

# Pre-signed URLs
aws s3 presign s3://bucket/file.pdf --expires-in 3600

# Bucket Configuration
aws s3api get-bucket-versioning --bucket bucket-name
aws s3api put-bucket-versioning --bucket bucket-name \
    --versioning-configuration Status=Enabled

# Lifecycle Rules
aws s3api put-bucket-lifecycle-configuration \
    --bucket bucket-name \
    --lifecycle-configuration file://lifecycle.json

🔗 Integration with AWS Services

Key AWS Service Integrations for anihpj
1. CloudFront (CDN)
# Django settings with CloudFront
AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN = 'd1234abcd.cloudfront.net'
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN}/static/'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN}/media/'

# Benefits:
# - 10x faster content delivery
# - 70% reduction in S3 costs
# - SSL/TLS encryption
# - DDoS protection
2. Lambda (Serverless Processing)
# Lambda function for image resizing
import boto3
from PIL import Image
import io

s3_client = boto3.client('s3')

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    bucket = event['Records'][0]['s3']['bucket']['name']
    key = event['Records'][0]['s3']['object']['key']
    
    # Download original image
    response = s3_client.get_object(Bucket=bucket, Key=key)
    img = Image.open(io.BytesIO(response['Body'].read()))
    
    # Resize to thumbnail
    img.thumbnail((200, 200))
    
    # Save back to S3
    buffer = io.BytesIO()
    img.save(buffer, 'JPEG')
    buffer.seek(0)
    
    thumb_key = key.replace('logos/', 'logos/thumbnails/')
    s3_client.put_object(
        Bucket=bucket,
        Key=thumb_key,
        Body=buffer,
        ContentType='image/jpeg'
    )
3. RDS (Database Backups)
# Automated RDS backup to S3
aws rds create-db-snapshot \
    --db-instance-identifier anihpj-db \
    --db-snapshot-identifier anihpj-snapshot-$(date +%Y%m%d)

# Export snapshot to S3
aws rds start-export-task \
    --export-task-identifier anihpj-export \
    --source-arn arn:aws:rds:us-east-1:123456789012:snapshot:anihpj-snapshot \
    --s3-bucket-name anihpj-backups \
    --iam-role-arn arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/rds-s3-export

🚀 Deployment & CI/CD

GitHub Actions Workflow for S3 Deployment
# .github/workflows/deploy-static-to-s3.yml
name: Deploy Static Files to S3

on:
  push:
    branches: [main]

jobs:
  deploy:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    
    - name: Set up Python
      uses: actions/setup-python@v4
      with:
        python-version: '3.11'
    
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: |
        pip install -r requirements.txt
    
    - name: Collect static files
      run: |
        python manage.py collectstatic --noinput
      env:
        AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}
        AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME: anihpj-static
    
    - name: Invalidate CloudFront cache
      run: |
        aws cloudfront create-invalidation \
          --distribution-id E1234ABCD \
          --paths "/*"
      env:
        AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID: ${{ secrets.AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID }}
        AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY: ${{ secrets.AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY }}

Security & Compliance
  • Certifications: SOC 1/2/3, PCI DSS, HIPAA, ISO 27001, FedRAMP
  • Encryption: Server-side (SSE) and client-side encryption
  • Access Logging: Track all S3 API requests
  • Object Lock: WORM (Write Once Read Many) compliance
  • Macie: Discover and protect sensitive data (PII)
✅ anihpj S3 Production Checklist:
  • ✅ Enable encryption at rest (SSE-S3/KMS)
  • ✅ Enable versioning on critical buckets
  • ✅ Block public access unless required
  • ✅ Configure CORS for web uploads
  • ✅ Set up lifecycle policies for cost savings
  • ✅ Enable access logging
  • ✅ Use IAM roles instead of access keys
  • ✅ Configure CloudFront for static files
  • ✅ Implement backup strategy (versioning + replication)
  • ✅ Monitor with CloudWatch metrics

📖 Glossary

Term Definition
Bucket Container for objects stored in S3 (like a top-level folder)
Object File stored in S3, consisting of data, metadata, and key
Key Unique identifier (filename/path) for an object within a bucket
Prefix Folder-like structure in object keys (e.g., resumes/user_123/)
Versioning Keep multiple variants of an object for recovery and rollback
Lifecycle Policy Rules to automate transition between storage classes or deletion
Pre-signed URL Temporary URL with embedded credentials for secure object access
Multipart Upload Upload large files in parts for better performance and reliability
Transfer Acceleration Use CloudFront edge locations to speed up uploads
CORS Cross-Origin Resource Sharing - allows web apps to access S3
SSE Server-Side Encryption - AWS encrypts data at rest
Glacier Low-cost archive storage class with retrieval times from minutes to hours

🎯 When to Use S3 for anihpj
Use S3 when:
  • ✅ Storing Django static files (CSS, JS, images)
  • ✅ User-uploaded files (resumes, logos, attachments)
  • ✅ Database backups and application archives
  • ✅ Serving files via HTTP/HTTPS API
  • ✅ Need unlimited, scalable storage
  • ✅ Want 99.999999999% durability
  • ✅ Integration with CloudFront CDN
Use EBS when:
  • ⚠️ EC2 root volumes and application data
  • ⚠️ Database storage (PostgreSQL, MySQL)
  • ⚠️ Need block-level access and low latency
Use EFS when:
  • ⚠️ Multiple EC2 instances need shared access
  • ⚠️ NFS protocol required
  • ⚠️ Concurrent read/write from multiple servers

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

🎓 Final Recommendation for anihpj:

Use S3 as your primary storage for all static files, user uploads, and backups. It's the most cost-effective, scalable, and durable option. Combine with CloudFront CDN for optimal performance.

Cost-Benefit: S3 costs 60-80% less than EBS/EFS while providing better durability and scalability. Perfect for Django applications with user-generated content.

Implementation Path: Local storage (Dev) → S3 (MVP) → S3 + CloudFront (Scale) → S3 + Lambda + CloudFront (Enterprise)

1. EC2 Instance Setup for Django

Launch Configuration
🚀 Launch EC2 Instance via AWS CLI
# Create security group for Django application
aws ec2 create-security-group \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --description "Security group for anihpj Django job portal"

# Allow HTTP, HTTPS, SSH access
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 22 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 80 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 443 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 8000 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# Launch EC2 instance
aws ec2 run-instances \
    --image-id ami-0c02fb55956c7d316 \
    --count 1 \
    --instance-type t3.medium \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair \
    --security-groups anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-jobportal-server}]'
User Data Script for Automatic Setup
📜 EC2 User Data Script
#!/bin/bash
# User Data Script for anihpj Django Job Portal

# Update system
sudo apt-get update -y
sudo apt-get upgrade -y

# Install Python, pip, and dependencies
sudo apt-get install -y python3 python3-pip python3-venv nginx git postgresql-client

# Create application directory
sudo mkdir -p /opt/anihpj
sudo chown ubuntu:ubuntu /opt/anihpj
cd /opt/anihpj

# Clone Django application
git clone https://github.com/your-username/anihpj.git .

# Create virtual environment
python3 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate

# Install Python dependencies
pip install -r requirements.txt

# Install additional packages for production
pip install gunicorn psycopg2-binary

# Create environment variables file
cat > .env << EOL
DEBUG=False
SECRET_KEY='your-secret-key-here'
DATABASE_URL=postgresql://username:password@anihpj-db.region.rds.amazonaws.com:5432/anihpj_db
ALLOWED_HOSTS=your-domain.com,your-ec2-ip
EOL

# Collect static files
python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Create systemd service for Gunicorn
sudo tee /etc/systemd/system/anihpj.service > /dev/null << EOL
[Unit]
Description=anihpj Django Job Portal
After=network.target

[Service]
User=ubuntu
Group=ubuntu
WorkingDirectory=/opt/anihpj
Environment=PATH=/opt/anihpj/venv/bin
EnvironmentFile=/opt/anihpj/.env
ExecStart=/opt/anihpj/venv/bin/gunicorn --workers 3 --bind 0.0.0.0:8000 anihpj.wsgi:application
Restart=always

[Install]
WantedBy=multi-user.target
EOL

# Enable and start the service
sudo systemctl daemon-reload
sudo systemctl enable anihpj
sudo systemctl start anihpj

# Configure Nginx
sudo tee /etc/nginx/sites-available/anihpj > /dev/null << 'EOL'
server {
    listen 80;
    server_name your-domain.com your-ec2-ip;

    location /static/ {
        alias /opt/anihpj/staticfiles/;
    }

    location /media/ {
        alias /opt/anihpj/media/;
    }

    location / {
        proxy_pass http://127.0.0.1:8000;
        proxy_set_header Host $host;
        proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Proto $scheme;
    }
}
EOL

# Enable nginx site
sudo ln -s /etc/nginx/sites-available/anihpj /etc/nginx/sites-enabled/
sudo rm /etc/nginx/sites-enabled/default
sudo nginx -t
sudo systemctl restart nginx

2. Django Application Configuration

Settings Configuration for Production
⚙️ Django Settings for EC2 (settings/production.py)
# anihpj/settings/production.py
import os
from .base import *

# Security Settings
DEBUG = False
ALLOWED_HOSTS = [
    'your-domain.com',
    'your-ec2-public-ip',
    'your-load-balancer-dns',
]

# Database Configuration for RDS
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj_db',
        'USER': os.environ.get('DB_USER'),

4. Auto Scaling Configuration

Auto Scaling Group for Job Portal
📈 Auto Scaling Setup
# Create Launch Template
aws ec2 create-launch-template \
    --launch-template-name anihpj-launch-template \
    --launch-template-data '{
        "ImageId": "ami-0c02fb55956c7d316",
        "InstanceType": "t3.medium",
        "KeyName": "anihpj-keypair",
        "SecurityGroupIds": ["sg-anihpj-jobportal"],
        "UserData": "base64-encoded-user-data-script",
        "TagSpecifications": [
            {
                "ResourceType": "instance",
                "Tags": [
                    {"Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobportal-instance"},
                    {"Key": "Environment", "Value": "production"},
                    {"Key": "Application", "Value": "jobportal"}
                ]
            }
        ]
    }'

# Create Auto Scaling Group
aws autoscaling create-auto-scaling-group \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --launch-template LaunchTemplateName=anihpj-launch-template,Version='$Latest' \
    --min-size 1 \
    --max-size 4 \
    --desired-capacity 2 \
    --target-group-arns arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:region:account:targetgroup/anihpj-tg/1234567890abcdef \
    --health-check-type ELB \
    --health-check-grace-period 300 \
    --vpc-zone-identifier "subnet-12345678,subnet-87654321"

# Create scaling policies
aws autoscaling put-scaling-policy \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --policy-name anihpj-scale-up \
    --policy-type StepScaling \
    --adjustment-type ChangeInCapacity \
    --step-adjustments MetricIntervalLowerBound=0,ScalingAdjustment=1
